The Shura After Umar and the Election of Uthman
Umar appoints a six-member consultative council for the next caliph.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the caliphate of Uthman was established through a consultative process that resulted in consensus.

Core Idea
Uthman's caliphate was a collective consensus, not a unilateral appointment.

After Umar's martyrdom, he left the caliphate to be decided by a consultative council of six senior Companions. This passage explains the process and how it led to the consensus election of Uthman, demonstrating the early Muslim community's commitment to consultation and agreement.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Umar's shura
Read the Arabic and translation to understand the context of the shura council appointed by Umar.
Focus on the composition and purpose of the council.
2
Identify the key actions in the process
Notice that Umar delegated the decision, the council delegated to Abd al-Rahman, and he chose Uthman. All accepted.
The process ended with consensus, which is emphasized.
3
Reflect on the principle of consensus
Understand that this consensus (ijma) established the legitimacy of Uthman's caliphate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم استشهد عمر رضي الله عنه وترك الخلافة شورى بين ستة عثمان وعلي وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وطلحة والزبير، وسعد بن أبي وقاص رضي الله عنهم، بمعنى أنهم يتشاورون فيما بينهم، ويعينون من هو أحق بها منهم بحسب رأيهم، وإنما جعلهم كذلك لأنه رآهم أفضل ممن عداهم وأحق بالخلافة ممن سواهم كما قال : مات رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو راض عنهم، إلا أنه لم يترجح في نظر عمر رضي الله عنه واحد منهم، فأراد أن يستظهر برأي غيره في التعيين، ولذا قال : إن انقسموا اثنين وأربعة فكونوا في الحزب الذي فيه عبد الرحمن، ثم فوّض الأمر خمستهم إلى عبد الرحمن ورضوا بحكمه، فاختار هو عثمان وبايعه بمحضر من عنهم، فبايعوه وانقادوا لأوامره وصلوا معه الجمع والأعياد، فكان إجماعا. ثم استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنه وترك الأمر مهملا ومجملا، فاجتمع أكابر المهاجرين والأنصار على علي كرم الله وجهه والتمسوا منه قبول الخلافة وبايعوه لما كان أفضل أهل عصره وأولاهم بالخلافة في دهره بلا خلاف في حقية أمره، وأما ما وقع من امتناع جماعة من الصحابة عن نصرة علي رضي الله عنه والخروج معه إلى المحاربة ومن محاربة طائفة منهم له كما في حرب الجمل وصفين فلا يدل على عدم صحة خلافته ولا على تضليل مخالفيه في ولايته، إذ لم يكن ذلك عن نزاع في حقيّة إمارته، بل كان عن خطأ في اجتهادهم حيث أنكروا عليه ترك القود من قتلة عثمان رضي الله عنه، بل زعم بعضهم أنه كان مائلا إلى قتله، والمخطئ في الاجتهاد لا يضلل ولا يفسق على ما عليه الاعتماد.
Then Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, was martyred and left the caliphate as a consultation (shura) among six: Uthman, Ali, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Talha, al-Zubayr, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, may Allah be pleased with them, meaning that they would consult among themselves and appoint the one most entitled to it from among them according to their opinion. He made them thus only because he saw them as the best of those besides them and most entitled to the caliphate over others, as he said: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, died while being pleased with them.' However, none of them was preponderant in the view of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, so he wanted to seek the opinion of others in the appointment. Therefore he said: 'If they divide into two and four, then be in the party that contains Abd al-Rahman.' Then he entrusted the matter to the five of them to Abd al-Rahman and they were pleased with his judgment. He chose Uthman and gave him the oath of allegiance in the presence of those with him, so they gave him allegiance and submitted to his commands and prayed with him the congregational and Eid prayers, so it was a consensus. Then Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, was martyred and left the matter neglected and ambiguous. So the senior Muhajirun and Ansar gathered around Ali, may Allah honor his face, and sought from him acceptance of the caliphate and gave him allegiance because he was the best of his time and the most entitled to the caliphate in his era without dispute regarding the truth of his affair. As for what occurred of a group of the Companions refraining from supporting Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, and going out to fight with him, and a party of them fighting him as in the battles of Jamal and Siffin, that does not indicate the invalidity of his caliphate nor the misguidance of his opponents in his governorship, for that was not due to a dispute over the truth of his leadership, but rather due to an error in their ijtihad wherein they denied his delaying the retaliation (qisas) from the killers of Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him. Rather, some of them claimed that he was inclined toward killing him. The one who errs in ijtihad is not deemed misguided nor sinful according to the relied-upon view.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage explains the historical succession after Umar and Uthman, and defends the caliphate of Ali while addressing the conflicts that arose among the Companions. It begins by describing the shura (consultation) appointed by Umar before his death. The six candidates were chosen because Umar considered them the best and most deserving, and he sought to delegate the decision to them with the guidance of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf. The result was the consensus on Uthman. After Uthman's martyrdom, the senior Companions unanimously chose Ali as the caliph due to his merit. The passage then addresses the objection that some Companions opposed Ali militarily in the battles of Jamal and Siffin. It clarifies that this opposition does not invalidate Ali's caliphate nor does it entail declaring the opponents misguided. The reason for their opposition was a difference in ijtihad: they criticized Ali for not immediately executing retribution for Uthman's killers, and some even suspected him of complicity. However, according to the sound principle, a mujtahid who errs is not considered sinful or misguided. Thus, the conflicts were based on legitimate ijtihad, not on denial of Ali's rightful leadership.

Key Terms
شورى
إجماع
خلافة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Umar directly appointed Uthman as caliph without consultation.
Correction: Umar set up a shura council and did not appoint anyone; the council chose Uthman by consensus.

Checkpoint
What was the outcome of the shura council after Umar?
A) Ali was chosen as caliph
B) Uthman was chosen as caliph
C) The council could not decide
D) Umar appointed someone else

Key Takeaway
The caliphate of Uthman was established through a consultative process that resulted in unanimous consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself in a disagreement with fellow Muslims, do you actively seek a shura-like process, or do you insist on your own opinion? This lesson shows that even the greatest companions submitted to collective wisdom. Where in your life can you practice more trust in group consultation, especially when the outcome is not your preference?
?
The companions accepted Abd al-Rahman's decision even though it meant Uthman, not Ali, became caliph. Is there a decision in your community or family that you have not fully accepted because it didn't go your way? What would it take for you to give sincere bay'ah to that decision and move forward in unity?
?
Umar died without imposing a successor, trusting the process of shura. Do you trust that Allah's guidance is present in sincere consultation among believers? What assumptions about leadership or authority prevent you from fully embracing this model today?

The Caliphate of Ali and the Principle of Ijtihad Error
Defends Ali's caliphate and explains opposition as ijtihad error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ali's caliphate was legitimate despite opposition, and how the principle of ijtihad error explains the actions of his opponents.

Core Idea
Opposition to Ali was due to ijtihad error, not denial of his right.

After Uthman's martyrdom, the senior Companions unanimously chose Ali as caliph. However, some Companions opposed him militarily. This passage clarifies that their opposition was not a rejection of Ali's leadership but a mistaken interpretation of his actions regarding Uthman's killers. It establishes the principle that a mujtahid who errs is not sinful.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on Ali's caliphate
Read how Ali was chosen and the opposition that followed.
Pay attention to the author's explanation for the opposition.
2
Analyze the reason for opposition
The author states it was due to ijtihad error regarding retaliation for Uthman's killers, not denial of Ali's right.
Note the specific claim that some thought Ali inclined to kill Uthman.
3
Learn the principle of ijtihad error
A mistaken mujtahid is not deemed misguided or sinful. This applies to the Companions who opposed Ali.
This is the key theological takeaway.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم استشهد عمر رضي الله عنه وترك الخلافة شورى بين ستة عثمان وعلي وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وطلحة والزبير، وسعد بن أبي وقاص رضي الله عنهم، بمعنى أنهم يتشاورون فيما بينهم، ويعينون من هو أحق بها منهم بحسب رأيهم، وإنما جعلهم كذلك لأنه رآهم أفضل ممن عداهم وأحق بالخلافة ممن سواهم كما قال : مات رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وهو راض عنهم، إلا أنه لم يترجح في نظر عمر رضي الله عنه واحد منهم، فأراد أن يستظهر برأي غيره في التعيين، ولذا قال : إن انقسموا اثنين وأربعة فكونوا في الحزب الذي فيه عبد الرحمن، ثم فوّض الأمر خمستهم إلى عبد الرحمن ورضوا بحكمه، فاختار هو عثمان وبايعه بمحضر من عنهم، فبايعوه وانقادوا لأوامره وصلوا معه الجمع والأعياد، فكان إجماعا. ثم استشهد عثمان رضي الله عنه وترك الأمر مهملا ومجملا، فاجتمع أكابر المهاجرين والأنصار على علي كرم الله وجهه والتمسوا منه قبول الخلافة وبايعوه لما كان أفضل أهل عصره وأولاهم بالخلافة في دهره بلا خلاف في حقية أمره، وأما ما وقع من امتناع جماعة من الصحابة عن نصرة علي رضي الله عنه والخروج معه إلى المحاربة ومن محاربة طائفة منهم له كما في حرب الجمل وصفين فلا يدل على عدم صحة خلافته ولا على تضليل مخالفيه في ولايته، إذ لم يكن ذلك عن نزاع في حقيّة إمارته، بل كان عن خطأ في اجتهادهم حيث أنكروا عليه ترك القود من قتلة عثمان رضي الله عنه، بل زعم بعضهم أنه كان مائلا إلى قتله، والمخطئ في الاجتهاد لا يضلل ولا يفسق على ما عليه الاعتماد.
Then Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, was martyred and left the caliphate as a consultation (shura) among six: Uthman, Ali, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, Talha, al-Zubayr, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, may Allah be pleased with them, meaning that they would consult among themselves and appoint the one most entitled to it from among them according to their opinion. He made them thus only because he saw them as the best of those besides them and most entitled to the caliphate over others, as he said: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, died while being pleased with them.' However, none of them was preponderant in the view of Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, so he wanted to seek the opinion of others in the appointment. Therefore he said: 'If they divide into two and four, then be in the party that contains Abd al-Rahman.' Then he entrusted the matter to the five of them to Abd al-Rahman and they were pleased with his judgment. He chose Uthman and gave him the oath of allegiance in the presence of those with him, so they gave him allegiance and submitted to his commands and prayed with him the congregational and Eid prayers, so it was a consensus. Then Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, was martyred and left the matter neglected and ambiguous. So the senior Muhajirun and Ansar gathered around Ali, may Allah honor his face, and sought from him acceptance of the caliphate and gave him allegiance because he was the best of his time and the most entitled to the caliphate in his era without dispute regarding the truth of his affair. As for what occurred of a group of the Companions refraining from supporting Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, and going out to fight with him, and a party of them fighting him as in the battles of Jamal and Siffin, that does not indicate the invalidity of his caliphate nor the misguidance of his opponents in his governorship, for that was not due to a dispute over the truth of his leadership, but rather due to an error in their ijtihad wherein they denied his delaying the retaliation (qisas) from the killers of Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him. Why did some Companions oppose Ali according to the passage?
A) They denied the legitimacy of his caliphate
B) They thought he was not the best for the role
C) They erred in ijtihad regarding retaliation for Uthman's killers

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone disagreeing with you about an Islamic matter, do you immediately assume they are misguided or sinful? How does the principle of ijtihad error challenge your assumption, and what will you do the next time you feel that urge?
?
Have you ever judged a fellow Muslim's action based on limited understanding without considering they might have a valid ijtihad? What steps can you take to withhold judgment and respect their reasoning?
?
The Companions themselves disagreed and even fought, yet they are praised. If you were in their position, would you have been able to disagree without condemning the other? What does your answer reveal about the state of your heart when facing conflict today?

The Thirty-Year Caliphate and the Status of Later Rulers
Uses hadiths to prove the true caliphate lasted thirty years and that later rulers were kings, not caliphs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses prophetic hadiths to argue that the true caliphate lasted thirty years and that later rulers, including Muawiyah, were kings, not caliphs, and how the term 'khalifa' is applied figuratively to later rulers.

Core Idea
The ideal caliphate ended after thirty years; later rulers are kings, not true caliphs.

This passage tackles a key theological and historical issue: who were the legitimate caliphs after the Prophet? By citing two famous hadiths, the author demonstrates that the true caliphate was limited to thirty years and that subsequent rulers, despite being recognized by the community, were not caliphs in the full sense. This lesson unpacks these arguments and their implications for our understanding of Islamic political authority.

Guided Path
1
The Thirty-Year Caliphate Hadith
Read the first proof: the hadith stating the caliphate after the Prophet lasts thirty years, then becomes tyrannical kingship. Note how the author links this to Ali's martyrdom exactly thirty years after the Prophet's death.
This hadith is well-known (mashhur) and forms the foundation of the argument.
2
The Hadith of Ammar ibn Yasir
Read the second proof: the hadith that Ammar will be killed by the rebellious band (al-fi'at al-baghiya). Understand how this implicates Muawiyah's side as being in the wrong during the Battle of Siffin.
This hadith is used to argue for the correctness of Ali's ijtihad and the error of Muawiyah's intention.
3
Refutation of a Counterargument
Examine the author's response to the claim that Ali effectively killed Ammar by bringing him to fight. Note Ali's powerful analogy: if that were true, the Prophet would have killed his uncle Hamza.
This refutation demonstrates the logical defense of Ali's position.
4
Conclusion and Clarification
Read the conclusion that Muawiyah and those after him were not caliphs but kings. Then see how the author addresses the objection about later caliphs like the Abbasids: the complete caliphate was only thirty years; after that, the term is used figuratively.
The author also mentions the Mahdi as a possible future true caliph.
5
Final Admonition from al-Suhrawardi
Read the quote from al-Suhrawardi, which reminds that disputes among the Companions were exploited by Satan and that we should honor all of them without delving into their conflicts.
This serves as a practical lesson to avoid sectarian division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومما يدل على صحة خلافته دون خلافة غيره الحديث المشهور : ((الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة ثم تصير ملكا عضوضا)) . وقد استشهد علي رضي الله عنه على رأس ثلاثين سنة من وفاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم، ومما يدل على صحة اجتهاده وخطأ معاوية رضي الله عنه في مراده ما صح عنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم في حق عمار بن ياسر ((تقتلك الفئة الباغية)) . ( وأما ما نقل أن معاوية أو أحدا من أشياعه قال: ما قتله إلا علي رضي الله عنه حيث حمله على المقاتلة، فروي عن علي كرم الله وجهه أنه قال في المقابلة فيلزم أن النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم قتل عمه حمزة، فتبين أن معاوية ومن بعده لم يكونوا خلفاء، بل ملوكا وأمراء. ولا يشكل بأن أهل الحل والعقد من الأمة قد كانوا متفقين على خلافة الخلفاء العباسية وبعض المروانية كعمر بن عبد العزيز، فإن المراد بالخلافة المذكورة في الحديث الخلافة الكاملة التي لا يشوبها شيء من المخالفة وميل عن المتابعة يكون ثلاثون سنة، وبعدها قد تكون وقد لا تكون؛ إذ قد ورد في حق المهدي أنه خليفة رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم والأظهر أن إطلاق الخليفة على الخلفاء العباسية كان على المعاني اللغوية المجازية العرفية دون الحقيقة الشرعية. ثم اعلم أن العارف السهروردي قال في الرسالة المسماة بـ إعلام الهدى وعقيدة أرباب التقى وأما أصحابه فأبو بكر رضي الله عنه وفضائله لا تنحصر وعمر وعثمان وعلي رضي عنهم، ثم قال: ومما ظفر به الشيطان من هذه الأمة وخامر العقائد منه ودنس وصار في الضمائر حيث ما ظهر من المشاجرة بينهم، فأورث ذلك أحقادا وضغائن في البواطن، ثم
And among the proofs for the validity of his caliphate over that of others is the well-known hadith: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years, then it becomes tyrannical kingship.' And Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, was martyred at the head of thirty years from the death of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. And among the proofs for the correctness of his ijtihad and the error of Muawiyah, may Allah be pleased with him, in his intention is what is authentically reported from him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, concerning Ammar ibn Yasir: 'The rebellious band will kill you.' As for what is transmitted that Muawiyah or one of his followers said, 'Only Ali killed him, may Allah be pleased with him, because he brought him to fight,' it is narrated from Ali, may Allah honor his face, that he said in response: 'Then it would follow that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, killed his uncle Hamza.' Thus it became clear that Muawiyah and those after him were not caliphs, but kings and princes. And do not be confused by the fact that the people of authority (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd) from the community were agreed upon the caliphate of the Abbasid caliphs and some of the Umayyads like Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, for what is meant by the caliphate mentioned in the hadith is the complete caliphate that is untainted by any opposition or deviation from following (the Sunnah), which is thirty years. After that, it may be and may not be; for it has been reported concerning the Mahdi that he is the caliph of the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace. The most apparent is that the application of 'khalifa' to the Abbasid caliphs was based on linguistic, figurative, customary meanings, not the legal reality. Then know that the gnostic al-Suhrawardi said in the treatise called I'lam al-Huda: 'The creed of the people of piety: as for his Companions, they are Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, and his virtues are endless, and Umar, Uthman, and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them.' Then he said: 'Among the things that Satan has gained from this community and has corrupted from the creeds and defiled, and has become in the innermost hearts, is what appeared of the altercation between them, which gave rise to hatreds and grudges in the interiors.' Then
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage provides proof for the validity of Ali's caliphate and the true nature of the caliphate after the Prophet. It begins by citing the famous hadith that the caliphate after the Prophet lasts thirty years and then becomes tyrannical kingship. Since Ali was martyred exactly thirty years after the Prophet's death, his caliphate falls within the true caliphate period. This hadith also serves to support the ijtihad of those who opposed Muawiyah. The passage then uses the hadith about Ammar ibn Yasir, who was killed by the 'rebellious band' (al-fi'at al-baghiya), to argue that Muawiyah's side was in error, since Ammar was killed in the battle of Siffin fighting on Ali's side. It refutes the claim that Ali killed Ammar by bringing him to fight, using Ali's own logical comparison: if that were true, then the Prophet would have killed his uncle Hamza by bringing him to battle. The conclusion is that Muawiyah and subsequent rulers were not true caliphs but kings and princes. The passage then addresses a potential objection: that the Muslim community's leaders (ahl al-hall wa al-'aqd) recognized the Abbasids and some Umayyads like Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz as caliphs. It explains that the 'caliphate' in the hadith refers to the complete, ideal caliphate that is free from opposition and deviation, which only lasted thirty years. After that, the term 'khalifa' is used metaphorically and conventionally, not in its legal sense, as in the case of the Mahdi who will be a true caliph. Finally, the passage quotes al-Suhrawardi, who reminds that the differences among the Companions were exploited by Satan to plant hatred, but the correct belief is to honor all of them without delving into their disputes.

Key Terms
الخلافة ثلاثون سنة
ملكا عضوضا
الفئة الباغية
اجتهاد
خليفة
المهدي
السهروردي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many believe that the Abbasid caliphs were true caliphs in the same sense as the first four, with the same religious authority.
Correction: The author clarifies that the complete, ideal caliphate ended after thirty years; later rulers are caliphs only in a figurative, customary sense, not in the legal reality.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, how long does the true caliphate last after the Prophet?
A) 20 years
B) 30 years
C) 40 years
D) Until the Day of Judgment

Key Takeaway
The true, ideal caliphate after the Prophet lasted only thirty years, and later rulers, including Muawiyah and the Abbasids, were not true caliphs but kings, with the title applied figuratively.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you look at the Muslim rulers or leaders today, do you simply accept their authority because they claim Islam, or do you evaluate them against the standard of the 30-year caliphate? What would it cost you to hold to that standard?
?
Have you ever held a grudge against another Muslim because of a historical or sectarian disagreement? How can you actively uproot that from your heart, knowing that Satan ‘gained from the community’ through these disputes?
?
If you were in a conflict today where you believed you were on the side of truth, would you be open to the possibility that you might be the ‘rebellious band’? How does the hadith of Ammar challenge your certainty about your own righteousness?

Al-Suhrawardi on the Origin of Sectarianism
Al-Suhrawardi explains how the Companions' minor inner traits were transmitted and corrupted by later people lacking spiritual hearts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Suhrawardi's psychological explanation for how later Muslims fell into sectarian conflict through the misinterpretation of the Companions' human traits.

Core Idea
Sectarianism arose from psychic affinity to ego traits, not the Companions' failings.

Al-Suhrawardi, a renowned gnostic, wrote a treatise on the causes of sectarian divisions among later Muslims. In this passage, he traces the problem to a subtle psychological process: the Companions, though pure-hearted, had occasional ego manifestations which they immediately rejected. Later followers, lacking the hearts to perceive the inner repentance, took these outer traits as models. This lesson unpacks that mechanism and its consequences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and its translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation to get the gist. Notice that al-Suhrawardi begins by praising the four caliphs.
2
Identify the three groups mentioned
Identify the Companions (with hearts), the intermediate people with egos but no hearts, and the later inheritors dominated by ego. Understand how each group relates to the ego traits.
3
Understand the mechanism of transmission
Focus on the sentence about 'a small part of the effects of their egos passed to people of egos who were devoid of hearts'. This is the key causal step.
4
Reflect on the purpose of the passage
Note that this explanation absolves the Companions of blame and places responsibility on later followers. Reflect on how this can prevent unfair criticism of the Sahaba.
This relates to a common misconception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن العارف السهروردي قال في الرسالة المسماة بـ إعلام الهدى وعقيدة أرباب التقى وأما أصحابه فأبو بكر رضي الله عنه وفضائله لا تنحصر وعمر وعثمان وعلي رضي عنهم، ثم قال: ومما ظفر به الشيطان من هذه الأمة وخامر العقائد منه ودنس وصار في الضمائر حيث ما ظهر من المشاجرة بينهم، فأورث ذلك أحقادا وضغائن في البواطن، ثم استحكمت تلك الصفات وتوارثها الناس فكثفت وتجسدت وجذبت إلى أهواء استحكمت أصولها وتشعبت فروعها. فيا أيها المبرأ من الهوى والمعصية اعلم أن الصحابة رضي عنهم مع نزاهة بواطنهم وطهارة قلوبهم كانوا بشرا، وكانت لهم نفوس وللنفوس صفات تظهر، وقد كانت نفوسهم تظهر بصفة وقلوبهم منكرة لذلك فيرجعون إلى حكم قلوبهم وينكرون ما كان في نفوسهم، فانتقل اليسير من آثار نفوسهم إلى أرباب نفوس عدموا القلوب فما أدركوا قضايا قلوبهم، وصارت صفات نفوسهم مدركة عندهم للجنسية النفسية، فبنوا تصرف النفوس على الظاهر المفهوم عندهم، ووقعوا في بدع وشبه أوردتهم كل مورد ردي، وجرعتهم كل شراب دني، واستعجم عليهم صفاء قلوبهم ورجوع كل أحد إلى الإنصاف وادعائه لما يجب من الاعتراف، وكان عدهم كانت محفوفة بأنوار القلوب، فلما توارث ذلك أرباب النفوس المتسلطة الأمارة بالسوء، القاهرة للقلوب المحرومة من أنوارها أحدث عندهم اليسير من صفات نفوسهم؛ العداوة والبغضاء.
Then know that the gnostic al-Suhrawardi said in the epistle called 'Ilam al-Huda wa Aqidat Arbab al-Tuqa': 'As for his Companions, they are Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him—his virtues are countless—and Umar, Uthman, and Ali, may Allah be pleased with them all. Then he said: Among the things by which Satan has prevailed over this community, infiltrating its creeds, defiling them, and becoming entrenched in consciences, is the conflict that appeared among them. This engendered hatreds and rancors in the innermost hearts. Then those traits became deeply rooted, inherited by people, became dense and embodied, and attracted to passions whose roots became established and branches branched out. So O you who are free from passion and sin, know that the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, despite the purity of their innermost and the cleanness of their hearts, were human. They had egos, and egos have traits that manifest. Their egos would manifest a trait while their hearts disapproved of it, so they would return to the judgment of their hearts and reject what was in their egos. Then a small part of the effects of their egos passed to people of egos who were devoid of hearts, so they did not grasp the matters of their hearts. The traits of their egos became perceptible to them due to psychic affinity. So they built upon the outward understanding of how egos act and fell into innovations and ambiguities that led them to every wicked place and made them drink every vile drink. The purity of hearts and the return of everyone to fairness and claiming what must be acknowledged became difficult for them. Their enemies [or 'their group'?] were surrounded by the lights of hearts. When those who inherited this were the people of dominating egos that command evil, overwhelming hearts deprived of their lights, the small part of their ego traits produced in them enmity and hatred.'
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is a psychological and spiritual analysis of how sectarianism originated among later Muslims, quoted from the gnostic al-Suhrawardi. It begins by affirming the immense virtues of the four rightly-guided caliphs. Then it explains the mechanism: the Companions, though spiritually pure, were human and had ego traits. When such traits occasionally surfaced, their hearts would immediately reject them and they would repent. However, later generations—people lacking spiritual hearts—only saw the outward manifestation of these ego traits and, due to a kind of psychic affinity, took them as a model. They built upon this superficial understanding, leading to innovations (bidʿah) and ambiguities (shubah). These people were deprived of the heart's purity that leads to fairness and confession. The original Companions were always surrounded by the lights of their hearts, but the later inheritors were dominated by ego and devoid of heart light, so the small residue of ego traits they transmitted resulted in enmity and hatred. The argument thus absolves the Companions of blame and places the responsibility on later followers who misinterpreted their actions.

شبه
أحقاد
ضغائن
الجنسية النفسية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think al-Suhrawardi is accusing the Companions of sin or conflict.
Correction: He clarifies that they always repented and that later people misinterpreted their momentary human weaknesses.

Checkpoint
According to al-Suhrawardi, what was the cause of enmity and hatred among later Muslims?
A) The Companions intentionally spread discord
B) The transmission of a small part of the Companions' ego traits to people without hearts
C) The hadith about Ammar ibn Yasir
D) The disagreement over the caliphate

Key Takeaway
Sectarian divisions among later Muslims arose from the misinterpretation of the Companions' human ego traits, not from any sin on their part.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you think about the Companions' ego traits that were rejected by their hearts, which trait in your own character do you often excuse despite knowing your heart disapproves? What specific step will you take today to reject it and return to your heart's judgment?
?
Al-Suhrawardi says later people inherited enmity from a small part of ego traits. Is there a grudge or hatred you are carrying that you may have inherited from family, culture, or community—even if you didn't personally experience the original conflict? Will you trace it to its ego-root and ask Allah to purify your heart from it?
?
The later people lacked spiritual hearts and so misinterpreted the Companions' outward actions. Where in your life might you be judging others based on outward appearances without seeking the purity of heart that leads to fairness? What would it cost you to assume good and seek the light of the heart instead?

Loving the Companions: Advice and Minimum Creed
Advice on loving Companions and minimum creed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proper attitude toward the Companions: maintaining equal love, avoiding public preference, and the minimum creedal requirement.

Core Idea
Love all Companions equally, but private preference is permitted.

This passage offers practical guidance for Muslims regarding the Companions. It balances the obligation of love with the allowance for personal preference, while emphasizing the foundational creedal point: accepting the caliphate of the four rightly-guided caliphs. The commentator adds a note about the rhetorical context.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully. Notice the structure: the author gives three pieces of advice, then concludes with the minimum creed. The commentator then clarifies the author's intent.
The Arabic text ends abruptly; the translator has inferred the meaning.
2
Identify the three pieces of advice
The author advises: 1) Refrain from involving yourself in disputes about the Companions. 2) Make your love for all equal. 3) If you have a preference, keep it a secret. Recognize that the author is setting out a practical approach for unity.
These three points are the core practical guidance.
3
Understand the commentator's clarification
The commentator points out that the author's advice is a diplomatic concession to opponents, not a statement that all Companions are equal in status. The author's own belief may differ, likely that some are superior (e.g., Abu Bakr). This distinction is important to avoid misunderstanding.
The passage ends mid-sentence; the commentator's full thought may continue on the next page.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قبلت النصح فأمسك عن التصرف في أمرهم واجعل محبتك للكل على السواء وأمسك عن التفضيل، وإن خامر باطنك فضل أحدهم على الآخر فاجعل ذلك أسرارك، فما يلزمك إظهاره ولا يلزمك أن تحب أحدهم أكثر من الآخر، بل يلزمك محبة الجميع والاعتراف بفضل الجميع ويكفيك في العقيدة السليمة أن تعتقد صحة خلافة أبي بكر رضي الله عنه وعمر وعثمان وعلي رضي الله عنهم، انتهى. ولا يخفى أن هذا من الشيخ إرخاء العنان مع الخصم في ميدان البيان، لا أن معتقده تساوي
If you accept the advice, then refrain from involving yourself in their affair and make your love for all equal, and refrain from preferring one over another. And if the preference of one over another occurs to your inner self, then make that your secret, for you are not required to show it, nor are you required to love one more than another. Rather, you are required to love all and to acknowledge the virtue of all. And sufficient for you in sound creed is to believe in the validity of the caliphate of Abu Bakr, may Allah be pleased with him, and Umar, Uthman, and Ali, may Allah be pleased with all of them. End. And it is not hidden that this is from the Sheikh as a loosening of the reins with the opponent in the field of exposition, not that his belief is that they are equal.
Source pages p. 134

Commentary
This passage provides practical guidance for a Muslim regarding the Companions. The author advises: if you accept the counsel, do not engage in disputes about them, maintain equal love for all, and avoid public expression of preference. If a preference arises inwardly, keep it private because showing it is not obligatory. The essential obligation is to love all Companions and acknowledge their virtue. The minimum requirement for sound creed is to affirm the rightful caliphate of the four rightly-guided caliphs in order. Then the commentator adds a note: this advice is a rhetorical concession to the opponent, not a statement of the Sheikh's own belief that all Companions are equal in status. The Sheikh's actual belief may be different (implying that some Companions are superior, e.g., Abu Bakr). The passage ends mid-sentence, likely continuing on the next page.

Love Follows Virtue and Permissibility of Extra Love for Ali
Love follows virtue; extra love for Ali permitted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that love for the Companions follows virtue in both general and detailed terms, and that extra love for Ali is permissible as a matter of the heart.

Core Idea
Love follows virtue, but the heart is not commanded.

This passage from the sharh addresses a sensitive topic: how to balance love for the caliphs, especially when one feels more love for Ali. The author first establishes that love follows virtue—in general we love all, in detail we recognize ranks. Then he cites a narration permitting extra love for Ali, using the Prophet's own words about matters beyond human control.

Guided Path
1
Understand the principle: love follows virtue
Read the first sentence: 'ثم الظاهر أن المحبة تتبع الفضيلة قلة وكثرة وتسوية'. Note that love is proportional to virtue—whether little, much, or equal.
This sets the foundation for the discussion.
2
Distinguish summary vs. detail
The author clarifies that in summary (إجمالاً) we affirm love for all, as in the Quranic verse. In detail (تفصيلاً) we recognize preferences as earlier explained.
The verse 'رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمْ وَرَضُوا عَنْهُ' is cited for the summary level.
3
Analyze the permission for extra love
Read the narration from al-Kurdari. It says if one acknowledges the caliphate and virtue of all caliphs, then saying 'I love Ali more' is not blameworthy. The Prophet's hadith about division among wives shows that matters of the heart are not fully in our control.
This narration provides an exception for personal inclination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الظاهر أن المحبة تتبع الفضيلة قلة وكثرة وتسوية، فتعين إجمالاً في مقام الإجمال كما قال الله سبحانه: رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمْ وَرَضُوا عَنْهُ، وتفصيلا في مقام التفصيل الذي تقدم من التفضيل والله الهادي إلى سواء السبيل. ثم رأيت الكردري ذكر في المناقب ما نصه : من اعترف بالخلافة والفضيلة للخلفاء وقال: "أحبّ علياً أكثر" لا يؤاخذ به إن شاء الله تعالى لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: هذا قسمي فيما أملك فلا تؤاخذني فيما لا أملك.
Then it is apparent that love follows virtue—few, many, and equal. So it is determined in summary in the place of summary as Allah said: "Allah is pleased with them and they are pleased with Him", and in detail in the place of detail which preceded of preferring. And Allah guides to the straight path. Then I saw al-Kurdari mention in al-Manaqib: "Whoever acknowledges the caliphate and virtue of the caliphs and says 'I love Ali more' is not to be held accountable, Allah willing, due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'This is my division in what I own, so do not hold me accountable for what I do not own.'"
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage addresses the relationship between love and virtue concerning the Companions, specifically the Four Caliphs. The author begins by stating that love follows virtue in quantity, whether little or much, and also in equality. Therefore, in a general context, we affirm love for all Companions as indicated by the Quranic verse 'Allah is pleased with them...' (Surah al-Bayyinah 98:8). But in a detailed context where ranking is discussed, we specify the order of preference as previously mentioned. Then the author cites a report from al-Kurdari that if someone acknowledges the caliphate and virtue of all caliphs but says 'I love Ali more,' such a person is not to be blamed, because the Prophet said regarding division of time among wives that he cannot be held accountable for what he does not own—meaning love is from the heart and not subject to command. Thus, extra love for Ali does not imply deficiency in love for the others.

التفضيل
الكردري

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Loving Ali more means you must hate the other caliphs.
Correction: The passage shows that extra love for Ali is permissible without deficiency in love for others, as love is not fully under human control.

Checkpoint

B) Acknowledging the caliphate and virtue of all caliphs
C) Total equality in love for all caliphs
D) Following the Prophet's division of time

Key Takeaway
Love follows virtue, but extra love for Ali is permissible as long as one acknowledges the caliphate and virtue of all caliphs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Shura After Umar and the Selection of Uthman
Al-Qunawi narrates the shura after Umar and deduces the validity of the two shaykhs' caliphate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the consultation after Umar's death led to Uthman's election and how this process confirms the legitimacy of the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar.

Core Idea
The shura after Umar was a model of collective decision-making and adherence to the prophetic way.

This passage recounts the historic consultation (shura) convened after Umar's death to choose the next caliph. It highlights the criteria used and the eventual choice of Uthman. The author then draws a lesson about the validity of the first two caliphs, showing that the companions held them in high regard.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration of the shura
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Notice the sequence of events: Umar's delegation, the committee, and the role of Abd al-Rahman.
The passage is a historical report, so pay attention to the chain of actions.
2
Identify the condition posed
Abd al-Rahman placed a condition on the candidates: to rule by Quran, Sunnah, and the way of the two shaykhs. Identify how Ali and Uthman responded differently.
Ali added a mention of his own ijtihad.
3
Understand the author's conclusion
Al-Qunawi states that this event is a clear proof of the validity of the caliphate of Abu Bakr and Umar and the companions' adherence to their way.
This is a key Sunni doctrinal point.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider how this narrative reinforces the legitimacy of the first three caliphs and the consensus of the companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال القونوي وإنما أجمعوا على إمامة عثمان لوجود شرائط الإمام فيه. وقد روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه ترك أمر الإمامة بين ستة أنفس: عثمان، وعلي وطلحة، والزبير، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وسعد بن أبي وقاص رضي الله عنهم، وقال: لا تخرج الإمامة منهم، فجعلوا الاختيار إلى عبد الرحمن بن عوف ورضوا بحكمه، يعني حين امتنع لنفسه من قبول هذا الأمر من أصله، بيد علي رضي الله عنه وقال: أوليك على أن تحكم بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وسيرة الشيخين، فقال علي: أحكم بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وأجتهد برأيي، ثم قال لعثمان مثل ذلك فأجابه، وعرض عليهما ثلاث مرات وكان علي يجيب بجوابه الأول وعثمان يجيبه إلى ما يدعوه، ثم بايع عثمان فبايعه الناس ورضوا بإمامته، وفي هذا دليل واضح على صحة خلافة الشيخين واعتقاد الصحابة إمامتهما وطريقتهما. وقول علي وأجتهد برأيي لا يدل على مجانبته إياهما، وإنما قال ذلك لأن مذهبه أن المجتهد يجب عليه اتباع اجتهاده ولا يجوز له تقليد غيره من المجتهدين، ومذهب عثمان وعبد الرحمن بن عوف أن المجتهد يجوز له أن يقلد غيره إذا كان أفقه منه وأعلم بطريق الدين، وأن يترك اجتهاد نفسه ويتبع اجتهاد غيره انتهى وهو المروي عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه.
Al-Qunawi said: They only agreed upon the imamate of Uthman because the conditions of an imam were present in him. It has been narrated that Umar left the matter of the imamate among six persons: Uthman, Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and said: The imamate should not go out from them. So they delegated the choice to Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and agreed to his judgment, meaning when he refrained from accepting this matter for himself from its root, to Ali he said: I submit to you on condition that you judge by the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of His Messenger, and the way of the two shaykhs. Ali said: I judge by the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger and I will exercise my ijtihad with my opinion. Then he said the same to Uthman and he answered affirmatively. He presented it to them three times; Ali answered with his first answer, and Uthman answered what he called him to. Then he gave allegiance to Uthman, so the people gave allegiance and were satisfied with his imamate. In this is a clear proof of the validity of the caliphate of the two shaykhs and the Companions' belief in their imamate and their way. And Ali's saying 'and I will exercise ijtihad with my opinion' does not indicate his avoidance of them. Rather, he said that because his school is that a mujtahid must follow his own ijtihad and is not allowed to imitate other mujtahids. The school of Uthman and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf is that a mujtahid may imitate another if he is more knowledgeable and more learned in the path of religion, and may leave his own ijtihad and follow the ijtihad of another. This ends, and it is the narration from Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed account of the consultation (shura) after Umar's death to select the next caliph. The author first states the consensus on Uthman's imamate due to his possessing the necessary conditions. Then the narrative is given: Umar appointed a committee of six. They delegated the decision to Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf. Abd al-Rahman asked Ali and Uthman whether they would rule according to the Book, Sunnah, and the way of the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar). Ali answered that he would rule by Book and Sunnah and would also apply his own ijtihad. Uthman agreed without adding the clause about ijtihad. After three attempts, the choice fell on Uthman. The author then explains that Ali's mention of ijtihad does not mean he considered the way of the two shaykhs insufficient; rather, it reflects his methodology that a mujtahid must follow his own reasoning. In contrast, Uthman's school allows a mujtahid to follow a more knowledgeable one. This difference in methodology is cited from Abu Hanifa. The passage defends the legitimacy and wisdom of the selection process.

Key Terms
إمامة
شورى
الشيخان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What was the condition Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf posed to Ali and Uthman?
A) To rule by the Quran and Sunnah only.
B) To rule by Quran, Sunnah, and the way of the two shaykhs.
C) To follow the opinion of the majority.
D) To abdicate in favor of the other.

Key Takeaway
The shura after Umar demonstrated the companions' commitment to the Quran, Sunnah, and the precedent of the first two caliphs, affirming their legitimacy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a decision that affects others, do you genuinely seek collective wisdom like the Companions did in the shura, or do you rely only on your own judgment? What would it take for you to trust a group process even when you have reservations?
?
The companions accepted the condition to follow the way of the two shaykhs. In your life, are you willing to submit to the guidance of pious predecessors, or do you always feel the need to add your own opinion? What might that say about your humility before the tradition?
?
Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf stepped aside from personal ambition to serve as a mediator. Is there an area in your life where you are clinging to control or leadership that you should delegate for the greater good? What is holding you back?

Ijtihad vs Taqlid Among the Companions
Al-Qunawi explains the different schools on ijtihad and taqlid among the companions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the methodological difference between Ali and Uthman regarding ijtihad and taqlid, and how this explains Ali's response during the shura.

Core Idea
Ali's ijtihad was a methodological stance, not a rejection of the two shaykhs.

After the shura narrative, Al-Qunawi addresses a potential misunderstanding: Ali's mention of his own ijtihad might be seen as distancing himself from the ways of Abu Bakr and Umar. He clarifies that this was due to a difference in legal methodology: Ali believed a mujtahid must rely on his own reasoning, while Uthman and Abd al-Rahman allowed imitation of a more knowledgeable person.

Guided Path
1
Read the explanation of Ali's statement
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Al-Qunawi explicitly states that Ali's words do not indicate avoidance of the two shaykhs.
2
Identify the two schools of thought
Notice that the passage presents two doctrines: Ali's school (obligation of ijtihad and prohibition of taqlid) and Uthman's school (permissibility of taqlid for a less knowledgeable mujtahid).
3
Understand the connection to Abu Hanifa
The passage ends by attributing Uthman's school to Abu Hanifa, showing that this view was adopted by the Hanafi school.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this methodological difference resolves apparent tension and upholds the respect between the companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال القونوي وإنما أجمعوا على إمامة عثمان لوجود شرائط الإمام فيه. وقد روي أن عمر رضي الله عنه ترك أمر الإمامة بين ستة أنفس: عثمان، وعلي وطلحة، والزبير، وعبد الرحمن بن عوف، وسعد بن أبي وقاص رضي الله عنهم، وقال: لا تخرج الإمامة منهم، فجعلوا الاختيار إلى عبد الرحمن بن عوف ورضوا بحكمه، يعني حين امتنع لنفسه من قبول هذا الأمر من أصله، بيد علي رضي الله عنه وقال: أوليك على أن تحكم بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وسيرة الشيخين، فقال علي: أحكم بكتاب الله وسنة رسوله وأجتهد برأيي، ثم قال لعثمان مثل ذلك فأجابه، وعرض عليهما ثلاث مرات وكان علي يجيب بجوابه الأول وعثمان يجيبه إلى ما يدعوه، ثم بايع عثمان فبايعه الناس ورضوا بإمامته، وفي هذا دليل واضح على صحة خلافة الشيخين واعتقاد الصحابة إمامتهما وطريقتهما. وقول علي وأجتهد برأيي لا يدل على مجانبته إياهما، وإنما قال ذلك لأن مذهبه أن المجتهد يجب عليه اتباع اجتهاده ولا يجوز له تقليد غيره من المجتهدين، ومذهب عثمان وعبد الرحمن بن عوف أن المجتهد يجوز له أن يقلد غيره إذا كان أفقه منه وأعلم بطريق الدين، وأن يترك اجتهاد نفسه ويتبع اجتهاد غيره انتهى وهو المروي عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه.
Al-Qunawi said: They only agreed upon the imamate of Uthman because the conditions of an imam were present in him. It has been narrated that Umar left the matter of the imamate among six persons: Uthman, Ali, Talha, al-Zubayr, Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf, and Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and said: The imamate should not go out from them. So they delegated the choice to Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and agreed to his judgment, meaning when he refrained from accepting this matter for himself from its root, to Ali he said: I submit to you on condition that you judge by the Book of Allah, the Sunnah of His Messenger, and the way of the two shaykhs. Ali said: I judge by the Book of Allah and the Sunnah of His Messenger and I will exercise my ijtihad with my opinion. Then he said the same to Uthman and he answered affirmatively. He presented it to them three times; Ali answered with his first answer, and Uthman answered what he called him to. Then he gave allegiance to Uthman, so the people gave allegiance and were satisfied with his imamate. In this is a clear proof of the validity of the caliphate of the two shaykhs and the Companions' belief in their imamate and their way. And Ali's saying 'and I will exercise ijtihad with my opinion' does not indicate his avoidance of them. Rather, he said that because his school is that a mujtahid must follow his own ijtihad and is not allowed to imitate other mujtahids. The school of Uthman and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf is that a mujtahid may imitate another if he is more knowledgeable and more learned in the path of religion, and may leave his own ijtihad and follow the ijtihad of another. This ends, and it is the narration from Abu Hanifa.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed account of the consultation (shura) after Umar's death to select the next caliph. The author first states the consensus on Uthman's imamate due to his possessing the necessary conditions. Then the narrative is given: Umar appointed a committee of six. They delegated the decision to Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf. Abd al-Rahman asked Ali and Uthman whether they would rule according to the Book, Sunnah, and the way of the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar). Ali answered that he would rule by Book and Sunnah and would also apply his own ijtihad. Uthman agreed without adding the clause about ijtihad. After three attempts, the choice fell on Uthman. The author then explains that Ali's mention of ijtihad does not mean he considered the way of the two shaykhs insufficient; rather, it reflects his methodology that a mujtahid must follow his own reasoning. In contrast, Uthman's school allows a mujtahid to follow a more knowledgeable one. This difference in methodology is cited from Abu Hanifa. The passage defends the legitimacy and wisdom of the selection process.

Key Terms
اجتهاد
تقليد
أبو حنيفة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's use of ijtihad meant he rejected the way of the two shaykhs.
Correction: It was a methodological principle: he believed a mujtahid must rely on his own reasoning, not that he disagreed with them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what was Ali's reason for adding 'I will exercise my ijtihad'?
A) He wanted to emphasize his independence.
B) He believed a mujtahid must follow his own reasoning and cannot imitate others.
C) He disagreed with the way of the two shaykhs.
D) He wanted to show off his knowledge.

Key Takeaway
Ali's addition of ijtihad was a reflection of his legal methodology, not a rejection of the precedent of Abu Bakr and Umar.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see someone taking a different position on a religious matter, do you immediately assume they are rejecting the authority of the pious predecessors, or do you consider that they may have a valid methodological basis? How can you train yourself to adopt the charitable outlook shown in this passage?
?
If you were in a situation where you had to choose between following a more knowledgeable person and acting on your own reasoning, what would be the basis of your decision? Do you have a consistent method, or do you act on convenience?
?
This lesson demonstrates that the Companions themselves differed on the permissibility of taqlid for a mujtahid. How does this reality challenge any tendency you have to label those who disagree with you as deviant? What concrete step can you take to increase respect for legitimate differences?

Understanding the Hadith on Following Abu Bakr and Umar
Analysis of the hadith and its interpretations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the hadith 'Follow the two after me' and how different companions interpreted its application.

Core Idea
A single hadith can be understood differently depending on one's role and evidence.

This passage examines a key prophetic hadith about the first two caliphs and the reasoning behind its varying interpretations among the companions. By analyzing the arguments of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf and Ali, we see how scholarly differences can arise from the same text.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its context
Start by reading the Arabic passage about the hadith 'Follow the two after me' and the initial response of Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf. Notice the general application he took.
The hadith is from the two Sahihs.
2
Examine Ali's possible interpretations
Consider the two ways Ali might have understood the hadith: either as directed to non-mujtahids, or he exempted himself based on another hadith about following the rightly guided caliphs.
Ali's reasoning shows careful consideration of evidence.
3
Reflect on the logical point
Think about the author's remark that one person cannot be both an imitator and imitated. This explains why Ali would not follow the hadith literally if he himself was a source of guidance.
This connects to the concept of ijtihad and taqlid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا سيما وقد ورد في الصحيحين: اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر. وعبد الرحمن بن عوف بعموم هذا الحديث وظاهره، ولعل عليا رضي الله عنه أوله بأن الخطاب لمن لا يصلح للاجتهاد، أو خصص نفسه لما قام عنده من دليل كقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين. فإنه لا شك أنه داخل فيمن يتعين تقليده، ولا يتصور أن يكون شخص واحد مقلدا ومقلدا. وأما بيعة علي رضي الله عنه فكما روي أنه لما استشهد عثمان هاجت الفتنة وقصد قتلة عثمان وأهل الفتنة الاستيلاء عليها والفتك بأهلها، فأرادت الصحابة تسكين هذه الفتنة ورفع هذه المحنة، فعرضوا الخلافة على علي رضي الله عنه فامتنع عليهم، وأعظم قتل عثمان ولزم بيته، ثم عرضوها بعده على طلحة فأبى ذلك وكرهه، ثم عرضوها على الزبير فامتنع أيضاً إعظاماً لقتل عثمان، فلما مضت ثلاثة أيام من قتله اجتمع المهاجرون والأنصار وسألوا علياً وناشدوه بالله في حفظ الإسلام وصيانة دار الهجرة للنبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فقبلها بعد شدة وبعد أن رآه مصلحة، لعلمهم وعلمه أنه أعلم من بقي من الصحابة وأفضلهم وأولاهم به فبايعوه.
Especially since it has been reported in the two Sahihs: "Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar." And Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf acted upon the generality and apparent meaning of this hadith. Perhaps Ali interpreted it as the address to those not qualified for ijtihad, or he specified himself due to evidence he had, such as his saying: "Adhere to my Sunnah and the Sunnah of the Rightly Guided Caliphs." For there is no doubt that he (Ali) is among those whose imitation is required, and it is not conceivable that one person is both an imitator and imitated. As for the allegiance to Ali, it is narrated that when Uthman was martyred, the tribulation rose, and the killers of Uthman and the people of tribulation intended to seize control and kill its people. So the Companions wanted to quell this tribulation and remove this ordeal. They offered the caliphate to Ali but he refused, magnifying the murder of Uthman, and stayed in his house. Then they offered it to Talha, who refused and disliked it. Then they offered it to al-Zubayr, who also refused out of respect for Uthman's murder. When three days passed after his murder, the Muhajirun and Ansar gathered and asked Ali, adjuring him by Allah to preserve Islam and protect the city of Hijra of the Prophet, so he accepted after difficulty and after seeing it as beneficial, because they and he knew that he was the most knowledgeable of the remaining Companions, the most virtuous, and the most deserving. So they gave him allegiance.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: the hadith about following Abu Bakr and Umar, and the circumstances of Ali's acceptance of the caliphate. First, the author notes that Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf applied the hadith 'Follow the two after me' in its general sense. Ali might have interpreted it differently, either as addressed to non-mujtahids or considered himself exempt based on another hadith about following the rightly guided caliphs, since he himself was one of them, and one cannot be both an imitator and imitated. Then the author narrates the events after Uthman's murder: a period of chaos, the Companions trying to find a leader, Ali initially refusing due to the gravity of Uthman's murder, and after three days he accepted after being implored. The passage emphasizes that Ali was the most knowledgeable and virtuous, and his acceptance was for the greater good.

Key Terms
الصحيحين
الاقتداء
الخلفاء الراشدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the hadith 'Follow the two after me' required all companions to blindly follow Abu Bakr and Umar without exception.
Correction: The passage shows that even a companion like Ali, who was a mujtahid, could interpret it differently based on other evidence, and he considered himself a source of imitation rather than an imitator.

Checkpoint
Why did Ali possibly not apply the hadith 'Follow the two after me' to himself?
A) He rejected the authenticity of the hadith.
B) He considered the command only for non-mujtahids.
C) He thought it was abrogated.
D) He preferred to follow his own opinion.

Key Takeaway
The hadith about following Abu Bakr and Umar was understood differently by companions based on their scholarly status and other evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read a command from the Prophet, do you automatically assume it applies to you, or do you honestly assess whether you are among those it addresses? How might this lesson change the way you approach hadith?
?
Are you willing to accept that learned scholars may interpret texts differently, even from the same evidence? Does your heart feel at ease with that, or does it create discomfort? What does that reveal about your own relationship with knowledge?
?
The passage says one cannot be both a follower and a followed. In your life, are you more often blindly imitating others without evidence, or are you setting an example for others? What step will you take today to move from being a blind follower to a conscious seeker of truth?

The Circumstances of Ali's Caliphate
Historical account of Ali's bay'ah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical events that led to Ali's acceptance of the caliphate after Uthman's murder.

Core Idea
Ali accepted the caliphate reluctantly only after intense pressure to preserve unity and Islam.

This passage details the chaotic period following Uthman's martyrdom and the efforts of the Companions to restore order. It highlights Ali's initial refusal and eventual acceptance after being implored by the Muhajirun and Ansar.

Guided Path
1
Read the narrative carefully
Read the Arabic passage describing the events after Uthman's murder. Note the sequence: the tribulation, the killers' intentions, the Companions' response.
This is a historical account, not a doctrinal proof.
2
Identify the key figures and their actions
Pay attention to the roles of Ali, Talha, and Zubayr. Notice that each was offered the caliphate but refused initially.
Their refusal was due to the gravity of Uthman's murder.
3
Understand Ali's final acceptance
After three days, the community (Muhajirun and Ansar) convinced Ali. Note the reasons: preservation of Islam and the city of Hijra, and Ali's merit as the most knowledgeable and virtuous.
Ali's acceptance was a reluctant concession for the greater good.

Two Views on Taqlid among Mujtahids: Ali vs. Uthman and Abd al-Rahman
Explains Ali's statement and two views on taqlid among mujtahids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two scholarly views on whether a mujtahid may imitate another mujtahid, and how each view is supported by hadith.

Core Idea
A mujtahid's ijtihad is his own, but he may follow a greater scholar.

The passage clarifies Ali's statement about striving with his opinion, showing it does not imply opposition to the earlier caliphs. Instead, it reveals a difference in methodology: Ali held that a mujtahid must follow his own ijtihad, while Uthman and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf held that a mujtahid may imitate a more knowledgeable colleague. The passage then explores how each side used prophetic hadith to support their position, ending with a reflection on whether a single person can be both an imitator and imitated.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage fully, then the English translation. Note the key terms: ijtihad, taqlid, mujtahid.
2
Identify the two views
Look for the two schools: Ali's view that a mujtahid must follow his own ijtihad, and Uthman/Abd al-Rahman's view that a mujtahid may imitate a more knowledgeable scholar.
This is the central doctrinal point.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Notice how Uthman used the hadith 'Follow the two after me' from Sahihayn, and how Ali may have interpreted it as addressing non-mujtahids or made an exception for himself based on another hadith about following the guided caliphs.
This shows how hadith can be interpreted differently.
4
Reflect on the final point
Consider the statement that a person cannot be both imitator and imitated. What does this imply about the status of the Prophet's companions?
The final word 'يتصور' may mean 'conceivable'—check the context.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقول علي وأجتهد برأيي لا يدل على مجانبته إياهما، وإنما قال ذلك لأن مذهبه أن المجتهد يجب عليه اتباع اجتهاده ولا يجوز له تقليد غيره من المجتهدين، ومذهب عثمان وعبد الرحمن بن عوف أن المجتهد يجوز له أن يقلد غيره إذا كان أفقه منه وأعلم بطريق الدين، وأن يترك اجتهاد نفسه ويتبع اجتهاد غيره انتهى وهو المروي عن أبي حنيفة رضي الله عنه فأخذ عثمان لا سيما وقد ورد في الصحيحين: اقتدوا باللذين من بعدي أبي بكر وعمر. وعبد الرحمن بن عوف بعموم هذا الحديث وظاهره، ولعل عليا رضي الله عنه أوله بأن الخطاب لمن لا يصلح للاجتهاد، أو خصص نفسه لما قام عنده من دليل كقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: عليكم بسنتي وسنة الخلفاء الراشدين فإنه لا شك أنه داخل فيمن يتعين تقليده، ولا أن يكون شخص واحد مقلدا ومقلدا يتصور
And the statement of Ali, 'I strive with my opinion,' does not indicate his opposition to them [Abu Bakr and Umar]. Rather, he said that because his school is that the mujtahid must follow his own ijtihad and is not permitted to imitate another mujtahid. The school of Uthman and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf is that the mujtahid is permitted to imitate another if that other is more knowledgeable than him and more learned in the way of the religion, and that he should abandon his own ijtihad and follow the ijtihad of another. That is the end of the saying, and it is what is narrated from Abu Hanifa, may Allah be pleased with him. So Uthman took [this view], especially since it has been reported in the Sahihayn: 'Follow the two after me: Abu Bakr and Umar.' And Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf [took this] based on the generality and apparent meaning of this hadith. Perhaps Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, interpreted it as addressing those who are not qualified for ijtihad, or he excluded himself based on evidence that came to him, such as his statement, peace be upon him: 'You must follow my sunnah and the sunnah of the rightly-guided caliphs.' For there is no doubt that he [Ali] is among those whose imitation is incumbent, and it is not conceivable that one person is both an imitator and imitated?
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage clarifies an apparent problem from Ali's statement. The author explains that Ali's statement does not show opposition to the earlier caliphs. He then presents two views on ijtihad: Ali's view that a mujtahid must follow his own ijtihad, and the view of Uthman and Abd al-Rahman that a mujtahid may follow a more knowledgeable mujtahid. This is attributed to Abu Hanifa. Then it discusses how the hadith 'Follow the two after me' supports Uthman and Abd al-Rahman's position. Ali, however, may have interpreted that hadith as addressing non-mujtahids, or he made an exception for himself based on the hadith about following the guided caliphs. The passage ends with a logical reflection: Ali cannot be both an imitator and imitated.

Key Terms
اجتهاد
تقليد
مجتهد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ali's statement indicates he disagreed with Abu Bakr and Umar.
Correction: The passage clarifies it is a difference in ijtihad methodology, not opposition.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the view of Uthman and Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf regarding a mujtahid?
A) He must follow his own ijtihad
B) He may imitate a more knowledgeable mujtahid
C) He must follow the consensus
D) He must ask a mufti

Key Takeaway
This passage shows that disagreement among the Companions on ijtihad methodology did not imply opposition, but rather different interpretations of textual evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you find yourself disagreeing with a scholar whose knowledge you respect, do you honestly assess whether you are qualified to hold that disagreement, or do you let pride in your own reasoning prevail? This lesson shows that even a mujtahid like Ali recognized limits.
?
The passage highlights that Uthman and Abd al-Rahman were willing to abandon their own ijtihad for the sake of following those more knowledgeable. Where in your own religious practice are you clinging to a personal opinion that you know contradicts a greater authority?
?
Ali's view required him to follow his own ijtihad, but he still followed Abu Bakr and Umar in outward practice. This shows that methodology of reasoning does not equal disagreement in action. How often do you conflate having a different interpretation with being righteously independent, when in fact your actions may still align with the majority?

The Caliphate of Ali and the Condition of Consensus
Narrates Ali's bay'ah and argues caliphate does not require universal consensus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the caliphate of Ali (ra) was valid despite lacking universal consensus, and how the early community established his leadership.

Core Idea
A caliph's legitimacy does not require unanimous agreement; a contract by qualified Muslims suffices.

This passage presents the historical circumstances of Ali's caliphate and extracts a key principle of Islamic political theology: that universal consensus is not a condition for the imamate. By examining the Companions' actions, we learn that the caliphate is established through the contract of some righteous Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Read the historical narrative
Read the Arabic passage and translation to understand the sequence of events after Uthman's murder. Notice how Ali initially refused and was eventually persuaded.
2
Identify the main doctrinal claim
Find the sentence that states the condition for the validity of the caliphate. The author argues it is not universal consensus but a contract by some qualified Muslims.
The key phrase is: 'بل متى عقد بعض صالحي الأمة لمن هو صالح لذلك انعقدت'
3
Understand the refutation of opposing views
Notice how the author refutes claims that Talha and Zubayr were coerced and that the absence of others invalidated Ali's caliphate. This reinforces the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما بيعة علي رضي الله عنه فكما روي أنه لما استشهد عثمان هاجت الفتنة وقصد قتله عثمان وأهل الفتنة الاستيلاء عليها والفتك بأهلها، فأرادت الصحابة تسكين هذه الفتنة ورفع هذه المحنة، فعرضوا الخلافة على علي رضي الله عنه فامتنع عليهم، وأعظم قتل عثمان ولزم بيته، ثم عرضوها بعده على طلحة فأبى ذلك وكرهه، ثم عرضوها على الزبير فامتنع أيضاً إعظاماً لقتل عثمان، فلما مضت ثلاثة أيام من قتله اجتمع المهاجرون والأنصار وسألوا علياً وناشدوه بالله في حفظ الإسلام وصيانة دار الهجرة للنبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم فقبلها بعد شدة وبعد أن رآه مصلحة، لعلمهم وعلمه أنه أعلم من بقي من الصحابة وأفضلهم وأولاهم به فبايعوه، وليس من شرط ثبوت الخلافة إجماع الأمة على ذلك، بل متى عقد بعض صالحي الأمة لمن هو صالح لذلك انعقدت، وليس لغيره بعد ذلك أن يخالفه، ولا وجه إلى اشتراط الإجماع لما فيه تأخير الإمامة عن وقت الحاجة إليها على أن الصحابة رضي الله عنهم لم يشترطوا فيها الإجماع عند الاختيار والمبايعة ثم الإجماع إذا خرج عن أن يكون شرطا لم يكن عدد أولى من عدد فيسقط اعتباره، وتنعقد الإمامة بعقد أحد، وبهذا يبطل قول من قال: إن طلحة والزبير بايعاه كرها وقالا: بايعته أيدينا ولم تبايعه قلوبنا، وكذا قولهم إن سعد بن أبي وقاص وسعيد بن زيد وغيرهم ممن يكثر عددهم قعدوا عن نصرته والدخول في طاعته؛ لأن إمامته كانت صحيحة بدون بيعة هؤلاء.
As for the oath of allegiance to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, it has been narrated that when Uthman was martyred, sedition flared up, and the killers of Uthman and the people of sedition intended to seize control of it and kill its people. So the Companions wanted to calm this sedition and remove this trial. They presented the caliphate to Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, but he refused them, magnified the murder of Uthman, and stayed in his house. Then they presented it to Talha, but he declined and disliked it. Then they presented it to al-Zubayr, but he also refrained out of reverence for the murder of Uthman. When three days had passed since his murder, the Muhajirun and Ansar gathered and asked Ali, imploring him by Allah to preserve Islam and protect the city of the Prophet's migration, so he accepted it after hardship and after seeing it as a benefit, because they and he knew that he was the most knowledgeable of the remaining Companions, the most virtuous, and the most entitled to it. So they pledged allegiance to him. It is not a condition for the validity of the caliphate that the whole community unanimously agree on it. Rather, whenever some righteous members of the community contract it for someone who is qualified for it, it is established. And no one else after that may oppose him. There is no reason to require consensus because it would delay the imamate when it is needed. Moreover, the Companions did not require consensus when choosing and pledging allegiance. Since consensus is not a condition, number is not preferred over number, so its consideration falls. And the imamate is established by the contract of one. And with this, the statement of those who say that Talha and al-Zubayr pledged allegiance to him under coercion and said, 'Our hands pledged allegiance but our hearts did not' is invalid, as is their statement that Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas and Sa'id ibn Zayd and others of many number refrained from supporting him and entering into his obedience, because his imamate was valid without the pledge of these people.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage narrates the events leading to Ali's caliphate and argues that the caliphate does not require universal consensus. It explains that Ali initially refused due to the gravity of Uthman's murder, but was persuaded. The key doctrinal point is that the caliphate is valid with the contract of some qualified Muslims, possibly even one. This refutes claims that Talha and Zubayr were coerced, and that the failure of others to pledge allegiance invalidates the caliphate.

Key Terms
بيعة
خلافة
إجماع
إمامة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: A caliph's legitimacy requires universal consensus (ijma') of all Muslims.
Correction: The passage argues that the caliphate is valid when some righteous Muslims contract it for a qualified person; universal consensus is not required.

Checkpoint
What does the author argue is sufficient for the validity of the caliphate?
A) Consensus of all Muslims
B) Contract of some righteous Muslims for a qualified person
C) Appointment by the previous caliph
D) Majority vote

Key Takeaway
The caliphate is validly established when some righteous Muslims contract it for a qualified person, without needing universal consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there a leader or authority in your life (at home, work, or community) that you resist accepting because you didn't personally choose them or because others around you disagree? How does this lesson's teaching that a valid contract by qualified individuals suffices challenge your reluctance? Will you now actively submit to that authority for the sake of unity and benefit?
?
Ali accepted the caliphate reluctantly, only after seeing it as a greater good. Are you holding back from taking on a responsibility (even an unwanted one) because you fear opposition or lack of universal support? What would it take for you to step forward, trusting that the contract of a few righteous people is enough?
?
The passage declares that 'no one else after that may oppose him.' Is there anyone in your life—a parent, teacher, leader—whom you are subtly opposing because you think their position wasn't fully legitimate? Will you now commit to changing your attitude and offering your full support, even if you have private reservations?
