Imam al-Ash'ari's Argument and His Turn to Sunni Islam
Al-Ash'ari poses a dilemma about three brothers to expose Mu'tazili inconsistency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Ash'ari used a logical dilemma to refute Mu'tazili rationalism and why it led him to embrace Sunni Islam.

Core Idea
Mu'tazili rationalism fails before a simple dilemma about divine justice.

This lesson recounts the famous dialogue between Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and his Mu'tazili teacher Abu Ali al-Jubba'i. The exchange reveals a critical flaw in the Mu'tazili understanding of divine justice and obligation, which ultimately prompted al-Ash'ari to abandon their school and champion Sunni orthodoxy.

Guided Path
1
Read the story carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the characters: al-Ash'ari, al-Jubba'i, and the three hypothetical brothers.
Pay attention to the precise wording of the questions and answers.
2
Analyze the dilemma
Identify the two objections al-Ash'ari poses. The first from the child, the second from the disobedient brother. See how al-Jubba'i's answer to the first leads to a contradiction when applied to the second.
The dilemma hinges on the Mu'tazili claim that Allah must do what is 'most beneficial' (al-aslah).
3
Reflect on the outcome
Consider why al-Jubba'i was speechless and how this exposed the inconsistency of Mu'tazili theology. Then note al-Ash'ari's conversion and his subsequent role in establishing Sunni creed.
This event marks a turning point in Islamic theological history.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إلى أن قال الشيخ أبو الحسن الأشعري لأستاذه أبي علي الجبائي: ما تقول في ثلاثة إخوة مات أحدهم مطيعا والآخر عاصيا والثالث صغيرا ؟ فقال : الأول يثاب بالجنة، والثاني يعاقب بالنار، والثالث لا يعاقب ولا يثاب قال الأشعري : فإن قال الثالث: يارب لم أمتني صغيرا وما أبقيتني إلى أن أكبر فأومن بك وأطيعك وأدخل الجنة؟ فقال : يقول الرب إني كنت أعلم منك أنك لو كبرت لعصيت فدخلت النار فكان الأصلح لك أن تموت صغيرا، قال الأشعري: فإن قال الثاني: يارب لم لم تمتني صغيرا لئلا أعصي فلا أدخل النار، ماذا يقول الرب؟ فبهت الجبائي، وترك الأشعري مذهبه واشتغل هو ومن تبعه بإبطال رأي المعتزلة وإثبات ما وردت ومضى عليه الجماعة، فسمّوا أهل السنة والجماعة.
Until the shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari said to his master, Abu Ali al-Jubba'i: "What do you say about three brothers: one died obedient, another died disobedient, and the third died as a child?" He said: "The first is rewarded with Paradise, the second is punished with Hell, and the third is neither punished nor rewarded." Al-Ash'ari said: "If the third says: 'O Lord, why did You let me die as a child? Why did You not keep me alive until I grew up so that I could believe in You, obey You, and enter Paradise?'" He said: "The Lord says: 'I knew that if you grew up, you would disobey and enter Hell, so it was better for you to die as a child.'" Al-Ash'ari said: "If the second says: 'O Lord, why did You not let me die as a child so that I would not disobey and enter Hell?' What does the Lord say?" Al-Jubba'i was dumbfounded. Al-Ash'ari left his school and he and his followers occupied themselves with refuting the opinion of the Mu'tazila and establishing what was transmitted and what the community (al-Jama'a) had followed, so they were called Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a famous argument between al-Ash'ari and his Mu'tazili teacher al-Jubba'i that led to al-Ash'ari's conversion to Sunni Islam. Al-Ash'ari presents a scenario of three brothers: one obedient, one disobedient, and one who died as a child. According to Mu'tazili doctrine, based on rational justice, Allah is obligated to reward the obedient and punish the disobedient, while the child receives no reward or punishment because he lacked moral accountability. Al-Ash'ari then poses a dilemma: if the child complains to Allah that he was not kept alive to have the chance to believe and enter Paradise, Allah responds that He knew the child would have disobeyed if he lived, so it was better for him to die. Then al-Ash'ari asks: what would Allah say if the disobedient brother asks why he was not made to die as a child to avoid punishment? Al-Jubba'i is left without a consistent answer. This exposes the irrationality of basing divine action on human notions of justice and obligation. Consequently, al-Ash'ari abandoned Mu'tazilism and devoted himself to upholding Sunni creed (what was transmitted and followed by the community), leading to the designation 'Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a'.

Key Terms
أبو الحسن الأشعري
أبو علي الجبائي
معتزلة
أهل السنة والجماعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think al-Ash'ari rejected all rational argument and relied solely on revelation.
Correction: In fact, al-Ash'ari used a rational dilemma to expose the incoherence of Mu'tazili rationalism, showing that reason itself leads to affirming Sunni theology.

Checkpoint
What did al-Ash'ari's argument demonstrate about the Mu'tazili doctrine?
A) That it was completely rational.
B) That it could not consistently account for divine justice in all cases.
C) That Allah is not just.
D) That children should be punished.

Key Takeaway
The dilemma of the three brothers shows that Mu'tazili obligations on Allah lead to contradiction, leading al-Ash'ari to embrace Sunni theology.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever held onto a belief or practice simply because it made logical sense to you, even when it contradicted clear revelation? What would it take for you to submit as al-Ash'ari did?
?
When your own reasoning conflicts with what you know is true from the Quran or Sunnah, do you trust your intellect or the transmitted truth? And what is the cost of choosing one over the other in your life?
?
Al-Ash'ari left his teacher and his established school because he realized his position was inconsistent. Is there a comfortable belief or habit you cling to that, if you examined honestly, you would find contradicts what Allah has revealed? Will you have the courage to abandon it?

The Origin of the Mu'tazila: Wāṣil's Secession
Narrative of the origin of the Mu'tazila and their naming.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the historical origin of the Mu'tazila sect and the meaning of their name.

Core Idea
A single secession gave the Mu'tazila their name—but they called themselves champions of justice and tawḥīd.

This lesson takes you back to the famous study circle of al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī, where a student named Wāṣil ibn 'Aṭā' broke away over a theological dispute. His departure not only gave birth to a new sect but also sparked a naming controversy that reveals much about their core beliefs. Let's explore the story and its doctrinal backdrop.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its English translation. Notice the sequence of events: Wāṣil's secession, al-Ḥasan's remark, and the naming.
Pay attention to the phrase 'قد اعتزل عنا' – it's the origin of the name.
2
Understand the doctrinal trigger
Wāṣil's position on the grave sinner (al-manzila bayn al-manzilatayn) is what caused the split. Reflect on why this intermediate position was controversial.
This issue is a major point of difference between early Islamic theological schools.
3
Compare the names
Note that outsiders called them 'Mu'tazila' (seceders) but they called themselves 'Ahl al-'Adl wa al-Tawḥīd'. Ask yourself: why would a group prefer a name that highlights their principles rather than their historical origin?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأصل هذه المنازعة أن رئيس المعتزلة واصل بن عطاء اعتزل مجلس الحسن البصري رضي الله عنه يقرر أن مرتكب الكبيرة ليس بمؤمن ولا كافر وأثبت المنزلة بين المنزلتين، فقال الحسن رضي الله عنه: «قد اعتزل عنا». فسُمّوا المعتزلة وهم سموا أنفسهم أصحاب العدل والتوحيد لقولهم بوجوب ثواب المطيع وعقاب العاصي على الله سبحانه ونفي الصفات القديمة عنه.
The origin of this dispute is that the leader of the Mu'tazila, Wāṣil ibn 'Aṭā', seceded from the circle of al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī, may Allah be pleased with him, determining that the committer of a major sin is neither a believer nor an unbeliever, and he established the station between the two stations. So al-Ḥasan, may Allah be pleased with him, said: 'He has seceded from us.' Thus they were called Mu'tazila, while they called themselves the people of justice and tawḥīd because of their saying that reward for the obedient and punishment for the disobedient are obligatory upon Allah, Exalted is He, and their denial of the eternal attributes from Him.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage is a historical narrative explaining the origin of the Mu'tazilite sect. The author begins by stating 'the origin of this dispute' refers to the disagreement over the status of a grave sinner (murtakib al-kabīra). Wāṣil ibn 'Aṭā', the head of the Mu'tazila, seceded from the study circle of al-Ḥasan al-Baṣrī by asserting that the grave sinner is neither a believer nor an unbeliever but in an intermediate position (al-manzila bayn al-manzilatayn). In response, al-Ḥasan said, 'He has seceded from us,' hence the name 'Mu'tazila' (those who secede). The author then notes that the Mu'tazila themselves adopted the title 'people of justice and tawḥīd' based on two core doctrines: first, that it is obligatory upon Allah to reward the obedient and punish the disobedient (i.e., they affirmed divine justice in a way that imposes obligations on God), and second, their denial of the eternal attributes (ṣifāt qadīma) from Allah, which they saw as compromising tawḥīd. This sets the stage for later Ash'ari refutations.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
مرتكب الكبيرة
المنزلة بين المنزلتين
عدل
توحيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Mu'tazila were named after their doctrine of justice (al-'adl).
Correction: The passage explicitly states they were named 'Mu'tazila' because of Wāṣil's secession (i'tizāl), although they themselves preferred the title 'people of justice and tawḥīd'.

Checkpoint
Why were the followers of Wāṣil ibn 'Aṭā' called 'Mu'tazila'?
A) Because they believed in the intermediate position
B) Because al-Ḥasan said 'He has seceded from us' when Wāṣil left his circle
C) Because they called themselves the people of justice
D) Because they denied the attributes of Allah

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila originated from Wāṣil ibn 'Aṭā's secession over the intermediate position for grave sinners, and their name reflects this historical event, though they self-identified by their core principles of justice and tawḥīd.

Abu Hanifa's Understanding of Irja'
Author clarifies why Abu Hanifa was called Murji' and quotes his view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Abu Hanifa was labeled a Murji' and how his actual view differs from the heretical Murji'a sect.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa's irja' was about deferring judgment, not denying sin.

This passage clarifies a common misunderstanding about Abu Hanifa's theological label. While some called him Murji', the text reveals his actual position: he deferred the final judgment of major sinners to Allah, while maintaining hope and fear for all believers. Let's examine his own words.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic passage once to get a sense of its flow. Then read the English translation to ensure understanding.
Notice the key term 'irja' is defined as deferral.
2
Understand the label 'Murji'
The passage states that Abu Hanifa was called a Murji' because he deferred the affair of the major sinner to Allah's will. Make sure you grasp the linguistic meaning of irja'.
This is a technical term; do not confuse with the heretical group that claimed sins do not harm faith.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's own statement
Read the quoted statement carefully. Notice that he expresses both hope and fear for both major and minor sinners, but emphasizes fear for the major sinner.
This shows his balanced view, unlike the extreme Murji'a who deny any punishment.
4
Distinguish from heretical Murji'a
Reflect on how Abu Hanifa's deferral differs from the belief that sin does not affect faith. The passage clarifies that his irja' is about postponing judgment, not nullifying consequences.
This distinction is crucial for understanding early Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اعلم أن القونوي ذكر أن أبا حنيفة رحمه الله كان يسمى مرجئا لتأخيره أمر صاحب الكبيرة إلى مشيئة الله تعالى والإرجاء التأخير، وكان يقول : إني لأرجو لصاحب الذنب الكبير والصغير وأخاف عليهما، وأنا أرجو لصاحب الذنب الصغير أخاف على صاحب الذنب الكبير، انتهى.
Know that al-Qunawi mentioned that Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, was called a Murji' because of his deferring the affair of the committer of a major sin to the will of Allah Almighty, and al-irja' is deferral. And he used to say: 'Indeed I hope for the committer of the major and minor sin and I fear for them both, and I hope for the committer of the minor sin [but] I fear for the committer of the major sin.' End.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'Murji' as applied to Abu Hanifa and clarifies his actual position. The author begins by stating that al-Qunawi mentioned that Abu Hanifa was called a Murji' because he deferred the judgment of a major sinner to Allah's will. The author then explains that 'irja' linguistically means deferral. He then quotes Abu Hanifa's own words expressing hope and fear for both the major and minor sinner, showing that his position is one of balanced hope and fear, not the heretical view that sin does not harm faith. Thus, the label 'Murji' as used by some is misleading.

Key Terms
مرجئ (Murji')
الإرجاء (al-irja')
صاحب الكبيرة (committer of major sin)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that being called Murji' makes Abu Hanifa a heretic.
Correction: The passage shows his irja' is merely deferring judgment to Allah, not denying punishment.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why was Abu Hanifa called a Murji'?
A) Because he said sins do not harm faith.
B) Because he deferred the affair of the major sinner to Allah's will.
C) Because he denied punishment for sins.
D) Because he rejected the Qur'anic verses on punishment.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's label as 'Murji' refers to his deferring judgment to Allah, not to a denial of sin's consequences.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim falling into a major sin, does your heart lean more toward condemning them or toward entrusting their fate to Allah? How can Abu Hanifa's attitude of both hope and fear reshape your own inner response? Will you consciously practice this balance starting today?
?
Have you ever misunderstood or mislabeled someone based on a single word or reputation? What does this lesson teach you about the danger of judging before understanding? What practical step can you take this week to avoid such hasty labeling?

Refutation of al-Jilani's Accusation
Presentation of accusation and its contradiction with Abu Hanifa's works.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author refutes al-Jilani's claim that Abu Hanifa held a corrupt belief on faith by showing its inconsistency with Abu Hanifa's own creedal works.

Core Idea
Al-Jilani's accusation against Abu Hanifa contradicts his own writings.

This lesson begins with an accusation against Abu Hanifa found in al-Ghunya by Shaykh Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, who claimed that Abu Hanifa's view on faith is corrupt. The author presents this accusation and immediately counters it by showing that it contradicts Abu Hanifa's own creedal works, specifically al-Fiqh al-Akbar, and the broader consensus of Sunni creedal books. We will examine the accusation and the author's initial rebuttal.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Jilani's accusation
Read the passage where al-Jilani claims that the Hanafiyya are among the non-saved sects because Abu Hanifa allegedly held that faith is knowledge and affirmation, and that his companions transmitted that he said faith is mere attestation without affirmation.
Notice the strong language: 'corrupt belief and decaying statement'.
2
Identify the author's refutation
The author points out that this accusation contradicts Abu Hanifa's own creed in al-Fiqh al-Akbar and other creedal books written on the disagreements between Ahl al-Sunna and the Mu'tazila.
3
Understand the contradiction
Reflect on why consistency matters in creedal works. The author argues that if al-Jilani's claim were true, it would oppose not only al-Fiqh al-Akbar but also the broader tradition of Sunni creedal writings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما وقع في "الغنية" للشيخ عبد القادر الجيلاني رضي الله عنه عند ذكر الفرق الغير الناجية حيث قال: «ومنهم القدرية، وذكر أصنافا منهم، ثم قال ومنهم الحنفية وهم أصحاب أبي حنيفة نعمان بن ثابت رحمه الله، زعم أن الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار بالله ورسوله، وبما جاء من عنده جملة على ما ذكر البرهوني في كتاب "الشجرة"، وهو اعتقاد فاسد وقول كاسد مخالف لاعتقاده في الفقه الأكبر»، وما نقله أصحابه أنه يقول: الإيمان هو مجرد التصديق دون الإقرار فإنه شرط عنده لإجراء أحكام الإسلام، ومناقض لسائر كتب العقائد الموضوعة للخلاف بين أهل السنة والجماعة وبين المعتزلة وأهل البدعة مع أن الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار هو المذهب المختار، بل هو أولى من أن يقال: الإيمان هو التصديق والإقرار لأن التصديق الناشئ عن التقليد دون التحقيق مختلف في قبوله، بخلاف المعرفة الناشئة عن الدلالة مع الإقرار وبالإقرار فإنه إيمان بالإجماع، وأما الاكتفاء بالمعرفة دون الإقرار وبالإقرار دون المعرفة فهو في محل النزاع كما قاله بعض أهل الابتداع.
As for what occurred in 'al-Ghunya' of Shaykh 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, may Allah be pleased with him, when he mentioned the non-saved sects, where he said: 'Among them are the Qadariyya,' and he mentioned types from them, then he said: 'And among them are the Hanafiyya, they are the companions of Abu Hanifa Nu'man ibn Thabit, may Allah have mercy on him. He claimed that faith is knowledge and affirmation of Allah and His Messenger and of what came from Him in entirety, as al-Barhuni mentioned in the book 'al-Shajara'. It is a corrupt belief and a decaying statement, contrary to his belief in al-Fiqh al-Akbar.' And what his companions transmitted that he says: 'Faith is mere attestation without affirmation, for it is a condition for him for the implementation of the rulings of Islam.' And it contradicts the rest of the creedal books written on the disagreement between Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a and the Mu'tazila and the people of innovation, while faith is knowledge and affirmation is the chosen doctrine. Rather it is more fitting than the statement that faith is attestation and affirmation, because attestation arising from imitation without verification is disputed as to its acceptance, unlike knowledge arising from evidence together with affirmation and with affirmation — for it is faith by consensus. As for being satisfied with knowledge without affirmation and with affirmation without knowledge, that is a matter of dispute, as some of the people of innovation said.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an accusation against Abu Hanifa found in al-Ghunya by Shaykh 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. The passage begins by citing al-Jilani's claim that the Hanafiyya are among the non-saved sects because Abu Hanifa allegedly held that faith is mere knowledge and affirmation, and that his companions transmitted that he said faith is mere attestation (tasdiq) without affirmation (iqrar). The author then critiques this claim, stating that it contradicts Abu Hanifa's own creed in al-Fiqh al-Akbar and other creedal works. He argues that the correct view is that faith is knowledge and affirmation, and that attestation without verification is disputed, whereas knowledge arising from evidence with affirmation is agreed upon. The passage thus defends Abu Hanifa against the accusation of holding a corrupt belief.

Key Terms
الغنية (al-Ghunya)
الحنفية (Hanafiyya)
الإيمان (faith)
المعرفة (knowledge)
الإقرار (affirmation)
التصديق (attestation)
الفقه الأكبر (al-Fiqh al-Akbar)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that al-Jilani's accusation is accurate and that Abu Hanifa indeed held a corrupt view on faith.
Correction: The author shows that the accusation contradicts Abu Hanifa's established creedal works, thus it is unfounded.

Checkpoint
On what basis does the author refute al-Jilani's accusation?
A) By citing a different definition of faith from al-Fiqh al-Akbar.
B) By showing that the accusation contradicts Abu Hanifa's other creedal books.
C) By claiming that al-Jilani is not a reliable source.
D) By quoting from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Al-Jilani's accusation against Abu Hanifa is refuted by pointing out its inconsistency with Abu Hanifa's own creedal works.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever believed an accusation against a scholar or a group without checking their actual writings? What would it cost you to verify before accepting such claims?
?
You may revere a teacher or a scholar whose opinions you accept uncritically. After seeing how al-Jilani's authority was contradicted by Abu Hanifa's own words, will you now examine the original sources of those you follow? What is stopping you?
?
Think of a conviction you hold about faith (iman) that you have never questioned. Could it be based on a partial or secondhand understanding? If the truth were different, would you have the courage to change your position based on clear evidence?

The Correct Definition of Faith According to Abu Hanifa
Author's positive argument on the definition of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's argument that faith consists of knowledge (ma'rifa) and affirmation (iqrar), and why knowledge arising from evidence is superior to mere imitation.

Core Idea
True faith is knowledge and affirmation, not blind imitation.

After refuting al-Jilani's accusation, the author presents the correct understanding of faith. He argues that faith is knowledge and affirmation, and that attestation (tasdiq) without verification is disputed. The key distinction is between attestation arising from imitation and knowledge arising from evidence, the latter being universally accepted as faith. This lesson unpacks that argument.

Guided Path
1
Identify the correct definition
The author states that faith is knowledge (ma'rifa) and affirmation (iqrar), and that this is the chosen doctrine (madhhab mukhtar).
2
Understand the dispute about imitation
The author explains that attestation (tasdiq) based on imitation (taqlid) without verification is disputed as to its acceptance, unlike knowledge based on evidence (dalala).
3
Grasp the consensus on evidence-based knowledge
Knowledge arising from evidence together with affirmation is faith by consensus, whereas being satisfied with only one component is a matter of dispute among innovators.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما ما وقع في "الغنية" للشيخ عبد القادر الجيلاني رضي الله عنه عند ذكر الفرق الغير الناجية حيث قال: «ومنهم القدرية، وذكر أصنافا منهم، ثم قال ومنهم الحنفية وهم أصحاب أبي حنيفة نعمان بن ثابت رحمه الله، زعم أن الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار بالله ورسوله، وبما جاء من عنده جملة على ما ذكر البرهوني في كتاب "الشجرة"، وهو اعتقاد فاسد وقول كاسد مخالف لاعتقاده في الفقه الأكبر»، وما نقله أصحابه أنه يقول: الإيمان هو مجرد التصديق دون الإقرار فإنه شرط عنده لإجراء أحكام الإسلام، ومناقض لسائر كتب العقائد الموضوعة للخلاف بين أهل السنة والجماعة وبين المعتزلة وأهل البدعة مع أن الإيمان هو المعرفة والإقرار هو المذهب المختار، بل هو أولى من أن يقال: الإيمان هو التصديق والإقرار لأن التصديق الناشئ عن التقليد دون التحقيق مختلف في قبوله، بخلاف المعرفة الناشئة عن الدلالة مع الإقرار وبالإقرار فإنه إيمان بالإجماع، وأما الاكتفاء بالمعرفة دون الإقرار وبالإقرار دون المعرفة فهو في محل النزاع كما قاله بعض أهل الابتداع.
As for what occurred in 'al-Ghunya' of Shaykh 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani, may Allah be pleased with him, when he mentioned the non-saved sects, where he said: 'Among them are the Qadariyya,' and he mentioned types from them, then he said: 'And among them are the Hanafiyya, they are the companions of Abu Hanifa Nu'man ibn Thabit, may Allah have mercy on him. He claimed that faith is knowledge and affirmation of Allah and His Messenger and of what came from Him in entirety, as al-Barhuni mentioned in the book 'al-Shajara'. It is a corrupt belief and a decaying statement, contrary to his belief in al-Fiqh al-Akbar.' And what his companions transmitted that he says: 'Faith is mere attestation without affirmation, for it is a condition for him for the implementation of the rulings of Islam.' And it contradicts the rest of the creedal books written on the disagreement between Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a and the Mu'tazila and the people of innovation, while faith is knowledge and affirmation is the chosen doctrine. Rather it is more fitting than the statement that faith is attestation and affirmation, because attestation arising from imitation without verification is disputed as to its acceptance, unlike knowledge arising from evidence together with affirmation and with affirmation — for it is faith by consensus. As for being satisfied with knowledge without affirmation and with affirmation without knowledge, that is a matter of dispute, as some of the people of innovation said.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage presents and refutes an accusation against Abu Hanifa found in al-Ghunya by Shaykh 'Abd al-Qadir al-Jilani. The passage begins by citing al-Jilani's claim that the Hanafiyya are among the non-saved sects because Abu Hanifa allegedly held that faith is mere knowledge and affirmation, and that his companions transmitted that he said faith is mere attestation (tasdiq) without affirmation (iqrar). The author then critiques this claim, stating that it contradicts Abu Hanifa's own creed in al-Fiqh al-Akbar and other creedal works. He argues that the correct view is that faith is knowledge and affirmation, and that attestation without verification is disputed, whereas knowledge arising from evidence with affirmation is agreed upon. The passage thus defends Abu Hanifa against the accusation of holding a corrupt belief.

Key Terms
الإيمان (faith)
المعرفة (knowledge)
الإقرار (affirmation)
التصديق (attestation)
التقليد (imitation)
الدلالة (evidence)
الإجماع (consensus)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that mere attestation (tasdiq) without verification is sufficient for faith.
Correction: The author clarifies that attestation from imitation is disputed; only knowledge from evidence with affirmation is universally accepted.

Checkpoint
Why does the author say that defining faith as attestation and affirmation is less appropriate?
A) Because attestation and affirmation are not part of faith.
B) Because attestation arising from imitation is disputed in acceptance.
C) Because the correct term is only knowledge.
D) Because the author prefers a different formulation.

Key Takeaway
Faith is defined as knowledge arising from evidence together with affirmation, which is accepted by consensus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is your faith built on knowledge and evidence from Allah's signs, or have you simply inherited it from your family and culture? What would it cost you to question your default beliefs and seek true ma'rifa?
?
Do you affirm with your tongue that 'there is no god but Allah' while your heart is empty of deep knowledge of His names and attributes? How will you actively pursue understanding so that your faith is not just an empty claim?
?
Imagine standing before Allah with a faith that is merely imitation – would that be sufficient? This passage warns that such faith is disputed. What concrete step will you take today to transform your taqlid into conviction based on evidence?

The Blameworthy Murji'a vs. Abu Hanifa's Middle Path
Author defines Murji'a and contrasts four positions on sin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the defining belief of the blameworthy Murji'a and how Abu Hanifa's position aligns with the Qur'an, distinguishing it from the extremes of Murji'a, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Sin can harm faith, but only Allah decides punishment.

The author introduces the Murji'a as a sect that claims sin does not harm faith, a dangerous exaggeration. He then contrasts their view with the balanced position of Abu Hanifa, rooted in the Qur'anic verse that places all sins except shirk under Allah's will. This lesson clarifies the correct Sunni stance on sin and punishment.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of Murji'a
Read the first two sentences identifying the Murji'a as those who say sin does not harm faith. Note their claim that no Muslim will be punished for major sins.
They are blameworthy innovators, not Qadariyya.
2
Contrast with Abu Hanifa's statement
Read how Abu Hanifa's statement matches Qur'an 4:48, putting sins under Allah's will. Understand that this is the middle path.
Contrast with Mu'tazila (obligatory punishment) and Khawarij (excommunication).
3
Identify the four positions
List the four groups: Murji'a, Abu Hanifa/Sunni, Mu'tazila, Khawarij. Note how each treats major sin.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المرجئة المذمومة من المبتدعة ليسوا من القدرية، بل هم طائفة قالوا: لا يضر مع الإيمان ذنب كما لا ينفع مع الكفر طاعة، فزعموا أن أحدا من المسلمين لا يعاقب على شيء من الكبائر، فأين هذا الإرجاء عن ذلك الإرجاء. قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله مطابق لنص القرآن، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النساء : ٤٨] ، بخلاف المرجئة حيث لا يجعلون الذنوب مما عدا الكفر تحت المشيئة، وبخلاف المعتزلة حيث يوجبون العقوبة على الكبيرة، وبخلاف الخوارج حيث يخرجون صاحب الكبيرة والصغيرة عن الإيمان. ثم اعلم أن مذهب المرجئة أنّ أهل النار إذا دخلوا النار فإنهم يكونون في النار بلا عذاب كالحوت في الماء، إلا أن الفرق بين الكافر والمؤمن أن للمؤمن استمتاعا في الجنة يأكل ويشرب وأهل النار في النار ليس لهم فيها استمتاع أكل وشرب وهذا القول باطل بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة من أهل السنة والجماعة وسائر المبتدعة، كما يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُمْ يَصْطَرِخُوْنَ فِيهَا [فاطر: ۳۷]، وقوله تعالى: كُلَّمَا نَضِجَتْ جُلُودُهُمْ ﴾ [النساء : ٥٦]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يُخَفَّفُ عَنْهُمْ مِنْ عَذَابِهَا [فاطر: ٣٦] ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَذُوقُوا فَلَنْ نَزِيْدَكُمْ إِلَّا عَذَابَانَ ﴾ [النبأ:٣٠]، وغير ذلك من الآيات والأحاديث البينات. وأما ما روي عنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم من أنه سيأتي على جهنم يوم تصفق الريح أبوابها وليس فيها أحد. واستدل به الجهمية وهم المرجئة الصرفة على فناء أهل النار، ففيه أن الحديث على تقدير صحته لا يعارض النصوص القاطعة بل هو مؤوّل بأن المراد بجهنم من طبقاتها المختصة بعصاة المؤمنين، فإنهم إذا خرجوا منها وذهبوا إلى الجنة تبقى صحراء ليس أحد فيها.
Then the blameworthy Murji'a from the innovators are not from the Qadariyya, but rather they are a group who said: No sin harms with faith just as no obedience benefits with disbelief. So they claimed that none of the Muslims will be punished for any major sin. Where is this 'irja' from that 'irja'? The statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, corresponds to the text of the Qur'an, which is His statement the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (al-Nisa' 48). Contrary to the Murji'a, where they do not place sins other than disbelief under [His] will, and contrary to the Mu'tazila, where they necessitate punishment for the major sin, and contrary to the Khawarij, where they expel the committer of the major and minor sin from faith. Then know that the doctrine of the Murji'a is that the people of the Fire, when they enter the Fire, they will be in the Fire without torture, like a fish in water, except that the difference between the disbeliever and the believer is that for the believer there is enjoyment in Paradise, he eats and drinks, while the people of the Fire are in the Fire with no enjoyment of eating or drinking for them. This statement is false by the Book, the Sunna, and the consensus of the Umma from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a and the rest of the innovators, as is indicated by His statement the Exalted: 'And they will cry out therein' (Fatir 37), and His statement the Exalted: 'Whenever their skins are roasted' (al-Nisa' 56), and His statement the Exalted: 'And torment will not be lightened for them' (Fatir 36), and His statement the Exalted: 'So taste, for We will not increase you except in torment' (al-Naba' 30), and other clear verses and hadiths. As for what was narrated from him (peace and blessings be upon him) that there will come a day upon Hell when the wind slams its doors and there is no one in it, and the Jahmiyya, who are the pure Murji'a, used it as evidence for the annihilation of the people of Hell. For it [the hadith], assuming its authenticity, does not contradict the definitive texts. Rather it is interpreted that what is meant by Hell is from its layers, the one specific to the disobedient believers, because when they come out of it and go to Paradise, it remains an empty plain with no one in it.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage distinguishes the true Murji'a (the blameworthy innovators) from Abu Hanifa's position, then refutes their doctrine. First, the author defines the Murji'a as those who claim that sin does not harm faith and that no Muslim will be punished for major sins, contrasting their extreme 'irja' with Abu Hanifa's moderate view which is based on the Qur'anic verse (al-Nisa' 48). The author then contrasts Abu Hanifa's view with the Murji'a, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij, showing that the correct Sunni position is that punishment for major sins is subject to Allah's will. Next, the author describes the Murji'a's bizarre belief that the people of Fire will be without pain, and refutes it with multiple Qur'anic verses that clearly describe severe and ongoing punishment. Finally, the author addresses a problematic hadith about Hell becoming empty, which the Jahmiyya use to argue for the annihilation of Hell. The author explains that even if authentic, it must be interpreted as referring only to the layer of Hell for disobedient believers, who will eventually be removed. Thus, the definitive texts about eternal punishment for disbelievers remain unchanged.

Key Terms
المرجئة (Murji'a)
المعتزلة (Mu'tazila)
الخوارج (Khawarij)
الكبيرة (major sin)
المشيئة (will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All Murji'a are the same as those who delay punishment without denying sin's harm.
Correction: The blameworthy Murji'a deny that sin harms faith, which is a distinct and extreme position.

Checkpoint
What do the blameworthy Murji'a claim about major sins?
A) They necessitate punishment.
B) They do not harm faith.
C) They cancel faith entirely.
D) They are forgiven only after repentance.

Key Takeaway
The Murji'a claim that sin does not harm faith is refuted by the Qur'anic verse that places all except shirk under Allah's will.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever secretly believed that your good deeds outweigh your sins, so you are safe? In light of this lesson, how does that resemble the Murji'a, and where do you actually place your trust?
?
When you see a fellow Muslim sinning openly, do you feel a desire for them to be punished—even if only in your heart? How does the Mu'tazila stance on obligatory punishment challenge you to surrender judgment to Allah's will?
?
Is there a sin you committed that makes you feel like you have lost your faith entirely? How does the Khawarij view of expulsion clash with the Qur'anic promise that Allah forgives what is less than shirk for whom He wills?

The False Doctrine of Painless Punishment in Hell
Refutation of Murji'a belief in painless Hell using Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Murji'a claim that Hell's inhabitants will be without suffering, and see how the Qur'an explicitly refutes it with verses about crying out, skin roasting, and unrelenting torment.

Core Idea
Hell is real, physical punishment – not a painless state.

The Murji'a went further, claiming that believers in Hell would feel no pain, like fish in water. This lesson presents the author's refutation using multiple Qur'anic verses that describe intense suffering. It reinforces that punishment in Hell is severe and constant for those destined to remain.

Guided Path
1
Read the Murji'a doctrine about Hell
Read the description that the people of Fire will be in the Fire without torture, like a fish in water. Note the exception they make for enjoyment.
This is an extreme and bizarre belief.
2
See the author's refutation
The author declares this false by Book, Sunnah, and consensus. Then he quotes four verses. Read each verse and note the type of punishment described.
Verses: crying out, skin roasted, no lightening, increase in torment.
3
Connect to the broader Sunni doctrine
Understand that these verses affirm real punishment, contrary to the Murji'a. This shows the consistency of the Sunni position.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

?

The Hadith of Hell's Emptiness and Its Correct Interpretation
Interpretation of the hadith about Hell becoming empty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how to interpret the hadith that Hell will become empty, without contradicting the perpetual punishment for disbelievers.

Core Idea
Hell's emptiness refers only to the layer for sinful believers, not the eternal Fire.

A hadith mentions that a day will come when Hell's doors slam shut with no one inside. The Jahmiyya (extreme Murji'a) use this to argue that Hell will eventually be empty for all. The author provides a key interpretation: the hadith refers specifically to the level of Hell for disobedient believers, who will be removed to Paradise, leaving that part empty. This protects the doctrine of eternal punishment for disbelievers.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and Jahmiyya claim
Read the hadith about Hell's doors being closed with no one inside. Note that the Jahmiyya use it as evidence for the annihilation of the people of Hell.
The hadith is problematic if taken literally.
2
See the author's resolution
The author says even if authentic, it does not contradict definitive texts. He interprets it as referring to the layer specific to sinful believers, who will eventually leave.
This preserves eternal punishment for disbelievers.
3
Understand the distinction
There are multiple layers of Hell. The hadith applies to the temporary punishment of sinful believers, not to the eternal abode of disbelievers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المرجئة المذمومة من المبتدعة ليسوا من القدرية، بل هم طائفة قالوا: لا يضر مع الإيمان ذنب كما لا ينفع مع الكفر طاعة، فزعموا أن أحدا من المسلمين لا يعاقب على شيء من الكبائر، فأين هذا الإرجاء عن ذلك الإرجاء. قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله مطابق لنص القرآن، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النساء : ٤٨] ، بخلاف المرجئة حيث لا يجعلون الذنوب مما عدا الكفر تحت المشيئة، وبخلاف المعتزلة حيث يوجبون العقوبة على الكبيرة، وبخلاف الخوارج حيث يخرجون صاحب الكبيرة والصغيرة عن الإيمان. ثم اعلم أن مذهب المرجئة أنّ أهل النار إذا دخلوا النار فإنهم يكونون في النار بلا عذاب كالحوت في الماء، إلا أن الفرق بين الكافر والمؤمن أن للمؤمن استمتاعا في الجنة يأكل ويشرب وأهل النار في النار ليس لهم فيها استمتاع أكل وشرب وهذا القول باطل بالكتاب والسنة وإجماع الأمة من أهل السنة والجماعة وسائر المبتدعة، كما يدل عليه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَهُمْ يَصْطَرِخُوْنَ فِيهَا [فاطر: ۳۷]، وقوله تعالى: كُلَّمَا نَضِجَتْ جُلُودُهُمْ ﴾ [النساء : ٥٦]، وقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا يُخَفَّفُ عَنْهُمْ مِنْ عَذَابِهَا [فاطر: ٣٦] ، وقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَذُوقُوا فَلَنْ نَزِيْدَكُمْ إِلَّا عَذَابَانَ ﴾ [النبأ:٣٠]، وغير ذلك من الآيات والأحاديث البينات. وأما ما روي عنه صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم من أنه سيأتي على جهنم يوم تصفق الريح أبوابها وليس فيها أحد. واستدل به الجهمية وهم المرجئة الصرفة على فناء أهل النار، ففيه أن الحديث على تقدير صحته لا يعارض النصوص القاطعة بل هو مؤوّل بأن المراد بجهنم من طبقاتها المختصة بعصاة المؤمنين، فإنهم إذا خرجوا منها وذهبوا إلى الجنة تبقى صحراء ليس أحد فيها.
Then the blameworthy Murji'a from the innovators are not from the Qadariyya, but rather they are a group who said: No sin harms with faith just as no obedience benefits with disbelief. So they claimed that none of the Muslims will be punished for any major sin. Where is this 'irja' from that 'irja'? The statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, corresponds to the text of the Qur'an, which is His statement the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive association with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills' (al-Nisa' 48). Contrary to the Murji'a, where they do not place sins other than disbelief under [His] will, and contrary to the Mu'tazila, where they necessitate punishment for the major sin, and contrary to the Khawarij, where they expel the committer of the major and minor sin from faith. Then know that the doctrine of the Murji'a is that the people of the Fire, when they enter the Fire, they will be in the Fire without torture, like a fish in water, except that the difference between the disbeliever and the believer is that for the believer there is enjoyment in Paradise, he eats and drinks, while the people of the Fire are in the Fire with no enjoyment of eating or drinking for them. This statement is false by the Book, the Sunna, and the consensus of the Umma from Ahl al-Sunna wa al-Jama'a and the rest of the innovators, as is indicated by His statement the Exalted: 'And they will cry out therein' (Fatir 37), and His statement the Exalted: 'Whenever their skins are roasted' (al-Nisa' 56), and His statement the Exalted: 'And torment will not be lightened for them' (Fatir 36), and His statement the Exalted: 'So taste, for We will not increase you except in torment' (al-Naba' 30), and other clear verses and hadiths. As for what was narrated from him (peace and blessings be upon him) that there will come a day upon Hell when the wind slams its doors and there is no one in it, and the Jahmiyya, who are the pure Murji'a, used it as evidence for the annihilation of the people of Hell. For it [the hadith], assuming its authenticity, does not contradict the definitive texts. Rather it is interpreted that what is meant by Hell is from its layers, the one specific to the disobedient believers, because when they come out of it and go to Paradise, it remains an empty plain with no one in it.
Source pages p. 151

Commentary
This passage distinguishes the true Murji'a (the blameworthy innovators) from Abu Hanifa's position, then refutes their doctrine. First, the author defines the Murji'a as those who claim that sin does not harm faith and that no Muslim will be punished for major sins, contrasting their extreme 'irja' with Abu Hanifa's moderate view which is based on the Qur'anic verse (al-Nisa' 48). The author then contrasts Abu Hanifa's view with the Murji'a, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij, showing that the correct Sunni position is that punishment for major sins is subject to Allah's will. Next, the author describes the Murji'a's bizarre belief that the people of Fire will be without pain, and refutes it with multiple Qur'anic verses that clearly describe severe and ongoing punishment. Finally, the author addresses a problematic hadith about Hell becoming empty, which the Jahmiyya use to argue for the annihilation of Hell. The author explains that even if authentic, it must be interpreted as referring only to the layer of Hell for disobedient believers, who will eventually be removed. Thus, the definitive texts about eternal punishment for disbelievers remain unchanged.

Key Terms
الجهمية (Jahmiyya)
المرجئة الصرفة (pure Murji'a)
فناء النار (annihilation of Hell)
طبقات (layers)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The hadith about Hell being empty means Hell will eventually be empty for everyone.
Correction: The hadith refers only to the temporary layer for sinful believers, not the eternal Hell for disbelievers.

Checkpoint
How does the author interpret the hadith about Hell becoming empty?
A) He rejects the hadith as unauthentic.
B) He interprets it as referring to the layer for disobedient believers.
C) He says it abrogates the verses about eternal punishment.
D) He says the verses are metaphorical.

Key Takeaway
The hadith about Hell's emptiness is interpreted as referring to the layer for sinful believers who will exit, not the eternal Hell for disbelievers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you were to die today, which layer of Hell would you fear being assigned to? How does that fear change what you will do tonight before you sleep?
?
The hadith speaks of believers who exit Hell after being purified. Does this hope make you complacent about a sin you keep repeating, or does it drive you to seek forgiveness and change now? Be honest with yourself.
?
The Jahmiyya used one unclear hadith to overturn clear Qur'anic verses on eternal punishment. Is there any aspect of your faith where you prioritize your own reasoning or a doubtful narration over the decisive Book? What will you do to correct that?

Sects and Disagreements
beginner
5 min
Abu Hanifa's Balanced View on Divine Forgiveness
Explains Abu Hanifa's agreement with Quran on forgiveness and contrasts with three sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Hanifa's position on divine forgiveness, based on Quran 4:48, differs from the Murji'ah, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij.

Core Idea
Forgiveness is Allah's will, not automatic punishment.

In this passage, the author presents Abu Hanifa's teaching on divine forgiveness, contrasting it with three extreme sectarian views. The Quranic verse (4:48) is the foundation. By examining each sect's error, we see the Sunni middle path.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the arguments of each sect.
Pay attention to the verse cited: Quran 4:48.
2
Identify the three sects mentioned
Find the Murji'ah, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij. Note the specific error attributed to each regarding sin and punishment.
The text contrasts each with Abu Hanifa's position.
3
Understand Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa aligns with the Quran: Allah does not forgive shirk but forgives lesser sins as He wills. This is the balanced view.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider how this balance avoids both extreme optimism (no punishment for any sin) and extreme pessimism (obligatory punishment or excommunication).
This is the Sunni 'middle path'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فزعموا أن أحدا من المسلمين لا يعاقب على شيء من الكبائر، فأين هذا الإرجاء عن ذلك الإرجاء. قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله مطابق لنص القرآن، وهو قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ اللهَ لَا يَغْفِرُ أَن يُشْرَكَ بِهِ وَيَغْفِرُ مَا دُونَ ذلِكَ لِمَنْ يَشَاءُ ﴾ [النساء : ٤٨] ، بخلاف المرجئة حيث لا يجعلون الذنوب مما عدا الكفر تحت المشيئة، وبخلاف المعتزلة حيث يوجبون العقوبة على الكبيرة، وبخلاف الخوارج حيث يخرجون صاحب الكبيرة والصغيرة عن الإيمان.
They claimed that no one among the Muslims is punished for any of the major sins. So where is this irja' from that irja'? The statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, is in accordance with the text of the Quran, which is His saying, the Exalted: 'Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him, but He forgives what is less than that for whom He wills.' [al-Nisa' 48], contrary to the Murji'ah, for they do not place sins other than disbelief under the will, and contrary to the Mu'tazila, for they necessitate punishment for the major sin, and contrary to the Khawarij, for they expel the committer of a major sin and a minor sin from faith.
Source pages p. 152

Commentary
This passage contrasts the correct Sunni position on divine forgiveness, as represented by Abu Hanifa, with three deviant sects: the Murji'ah, the Mu'tazila, and the Khawarij. The author begins by referencing an extreme Murji'ah claim that no Muslim is punished for any major sin, which is a form of irja'. He then presents Abu Hanifa's position as matching the Quranic verse (4:48), which states that Allah does not forgive shirk but may forgive anything else as He wills. This is opposed to the Murji'ah, who exclude all sins other than shirk from being under Allah's will (i.e., they claim that believers are not punished at all, which is the extreme of irja'); opposed to the Mu'tazila, who make punishment obligatory for major sins (thus denying that Allah may forgive them); and opposed to the Khawarij, who declare that a Muslim who commits a major or minor sin is expelled from faith (i.e., becomes a disbeliever). Thus the Sunni position is the balanced middle: major sins may be forgiven if Allah wills, but the believer is not necessarily expelled from faith.

Key Terms
مرجئة
معتزلة
خوارج
كبائر
مشيئة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That Abu Hanifa's position is identical to the Murji'ah's because both allow forgiveness.
Correction: Abu Hanifa differs because he does not deny the possibility of punishment for major sins; punishment is under Allah's will, not automatic forgiveness.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the position of Abu Hanifa regarding the forgiveness of major sins?
A) Major sins are never forgiven.
B) Major sins are always forgiven for believers.
C) Major sins are under Allah's will, He may forgive them or not, except shirk.
D) Major sins necessitate punishment in Hell.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view on forgiveness is the balanced Sunni position: major sins are under Allah's will, unlike the extremes of the Murji'ah, Mu'tazila, and Khawarij.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
After learning that Abu Hanifa holds the balanced view that major sins are under Allah's will, do you realize that you might have been falling into the extreme of either presumption or despair? Which extreme do you lean towards, and what will you do today to correct it?
?
How does the knowledge that Allah may punish or forgive major sins as He wills change the way you think about your own hidden sins? Are you using this as a license to sin or as a motivation to repent sincerely?
?
This passage contrasts your view of forgiveness with that of three deviant sects. Which of those three positions have you unintentionally adopted in your heart towards others? What step will you take to align your heart with the Quran and the balanced Sunni path?
